O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my very dear children, I have completed this book which is the last of medical science, its fulfillment, and have finished it through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And since the work of hands is closely guarded in our region and unknown everywhere, the knowledge has decayed and been lost, and there remains no stronger evidence than the small descriptions in old books about what the hands have done.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this, error and vanity have arisen, and thoughts are closed, and knowledge is separated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	It seems to me that I want to revive this treatise entirely by ordering it according to the way of exposition and explanation, and in a concise manner.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	and I will bring together the forms of cautery instruments and other tools for this work with their appropriate explanations and preparations, as is required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes to master this science of anatomy, as Galen says, that he know the judgment of the members, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones and nerves and blood vessels, and the number of them, and the movement and resting of veins and arteries, and from where they come.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And Hippocrates says that the name is not important, but the work is powerful.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and especially in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above, risks falling into error and misleading others.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	for I have often seen many who delve into this science without any knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	Because I have seen a foolish craze that cauterizes the abscess of a woman's neck or collarbone, cauterizing the arteries of her neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	for this causes so much blood that the woman dies in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans;	And he also showed me another wonder where he treated a stone from an old man, and the stone was great.
si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	if it removes a piece of the bladder with it, and it became infected within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; I knew well that if they attempted to remove it, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie;	And I saw another wonder where he took care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg and with the break came an injury.
et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine;	and the ignorant doctors tighten the break on the injury as if by strong force, and they do not leave any gap for the wound, and they leave it in that state.
et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie;	and he commands that he does not dislocate it again;
et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	and waits until the leg is completely swollen and painful, and it comes to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe;	I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come and dislocate the leg;
et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	and when I saw it dislocated, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner;	But any attempt at correction was already confirmed or the member was beyond repair.
et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	and does not cease the corruption of the limb as long as the member is completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I also saw another wonder that the abscess, which had been healed, suddenly became inflamed due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is free from black bile, it does not need to be cut with iron unless it is in a part that can be entirely removed without leaving any corrupted tissue.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions:	And for this reason, dear child, it is necessary for you to know that the art of healing is divided into two parts:
c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions;	that is to say, work where there is danger in many positions;
et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	and I will show, in each part of this book, where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	For this reason, it is important for you to guard against it, so that the foolish gaze cannot speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez;	If you take up your weapons in courage, and confront your enemies lightly but resolutely, and use the best method, through the grace of God, you will attain salvation and be happy.
et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit;	and leave the fearful diseases of sorrow behind,
et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	and cast away your weapons that cause you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens:	Galen does not speak of any of his warnings:
«Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Do not take any foul disease too seriously, unless you are called a fool for it.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatment according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez;	The first chapters deal with fire cautery and medicinal remedies for ague (malaria), and the chapters are ordered from the head to the feet.
et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	and the shapes of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything necessary for the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses;	The second chapter deals with cutting and piercing, as well as the use of suction cups and incisions, and the extraction of arrows, and similar procedures.
et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	and it details the ordering of chapters and the shapes of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses;	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar conditions.
et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	and it details the order from the most severe cases down to milder ones, as well as the shapes of instruments used.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, as we remember the work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of the aid and the harm or benefit of each condition.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus;	I say that the qualities of aid and its harmful effects are the longest discourse and the most subtle science, with secret answers.
et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu;	and of these things, many wise ones spoke and agreed.
et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	and I will be content with few of my words, for I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions:	I say that cautery helps universally wherever it has matter, whether it is in two or more complexes:
c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	This is to know: a hot complexion due to material, and a dry complexion without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide;	In a hot and dry complexion, combining material, they devised nothing and said that fire treatment is great help.
et li autre dirent le contraire:	and the others said the opposite:
que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	that fire treatment is not worth for ailments that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour;	For nature of fire is hot, and it must not be treated with heat from a hot ailment through warmth or dryness;
et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	and it helps greatly to cure hot and dry diseases that come upon the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the color of fire, you perceive the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens;	And in every case, no one should intervene unless they have tried it themselves, and know from long experience the chapter of cautery, and the diversity of human complexions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the remedies and the passage of time.
des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	we have only fear of other complexions, especially for cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all agreed and consented to the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, child, that cauterization combines fire in a way that is part of healing secrets and, moreover, offers greater gentleness than medicinal burning.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not come from outside unless it affects a hot member, and it does not harm any other member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation;	Burning medications come from one part of the body to another, causing illnesses of sorrow without healing.
et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	and by chance awakens the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	He does not waste it for its nobility and the goodness of its nature, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses;	And this is what I have found through experience and the length of my service and study in the art, and it was about the truth of the things.
et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant;	and for that I apologize for the length of the speech, because I do not like to deprive you of the secret that is revealed by fire, and the quality of the work, how it defeats bodily illnesses, as the philosopher demonstrates in proving.
or le recevez en vos pensees.	or receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agree on the time when cauterization must be performed, and carefully select the instruments.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere;	And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm causing pain is removed by the help of cautery.
et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	and indeed, cautery is for necessary and urgent pain, rather than waiting for greater harm to come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire;	And never think, dear child, as they do the foolish ones;
car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue;	Because the disease which is healed by cautery has no recurrence;
et il le dient ensi;	and thus it should be done;
mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	but it is not always as they should care for it, because cautery is only a medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors which are the cause of pain, and acts more swiftly than other medicines because of its virtue and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut;	And another powerful thing is that the disease comes according to the state of the patient and the place of the illness and its virtue;
et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie;	and they are assembled within him the excesses through the acquisition of meats and similar things, unless cauterization is administered to him where there is little excess and moisture, as with cautery for dense pain and similar things, and such pain does not return.
mais ce avient poc.	but this rarely happens.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir;	And many people do not understand at all why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true.
mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	but they do not believe that cautery has any value after medicine, but their intent is false, for when we administer remedies in any illness and they are ineffective, then we resort to cautery, which does have value.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cautery is the last of medicine, not at all according to the opinion of wise men.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance;	The ancients said that gold instruments for cautery are more powerful than those of iron, and they did not call them harsh except for the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance.
et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes;	and they said that gold in cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true, as I have tested it, and I have found that it is indeed harmful to no one.
et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	and gold cauterization is more effective than iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez;	However, when you heat gold instruments, you are not certain if it is heated by the color of gold, and it can cool down at any moment.
et s’on le chaufe trop;	and if he warms himself too much;
si font au feu;	if he does over a fire;
et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	and thus he has enough obstruction.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use the fire cautery that we have equipped for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now therefore I have ordered this chapter from the beginning to the end, so that the path may be easier to follow.
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	Fire cautery should be applied to the head with moisture and cold, and there are many ailments caused by this method, known as "soda", due to the descent of humors from the head to the limbs and ears, and also due to dreams, toothaches, throat pain, and particularly, diseases arising from coldness, such as paralysis, soda (a term likely referring to a type of stroke), apoplexy, and similar ailments.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir;	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is purged with a solvent medicine, purifying the third or fourth nerve affected, according to the virtue and age, and the patient's tolerance of the pain.
et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	and then makes the patient's head relax.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis;	And then make him sit crossed between your hands, placing his hands on some weight.
aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz;	after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes;
et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	and hold there with your two middle fingers; if blood comes out, then heat the cautery called "olive" whose shape is as follows:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant;	And place it on the dislocated joint marked with ink, and move your hand down and pull out gently, slightly disturbing it.
puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit;	then gently take your hand away, and relax the joint if you see a small bone out of place.
et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit;	and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you can see the bone as I have told you.
aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors;	after taking a little string, fill it with hard and soft cotton, place it over the joint, and leave it for three days.
aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre;	after that, apply soft cotton soaked in butter;
et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	and let them grow until the burn is healed;
aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing, dress the wound with "tetra-formula" as long as it is clean.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge;	And the elders said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it will fester;
et por ce si aide mues.	and for this reason, help is sought.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that one should not let the fire cautery burn off any part of the bone, and then remove what is burned from the bone, and it will be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors;	And he advised that the cautery should be left on for a long time, and to press so hard that one might even break the bone as women do when they give birth so that the humors are forced out.
et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte;	and one must leave the wound open for a long time.
aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	after that one must clean and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor;	And these two methods of cautery do not seem very good to me in every way, except for when they are used on people who have no choice.
et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier;	and it seems to me that I must leave it alone.
car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres;	for the flesh is weakened by continuous solutions of moisture, as we testify in other members.
et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	and also when the patient's shoulder is weak by nature, and the first appearance of treatment is more safe and gentle for me, and from this practice I achieve whole healing then together.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres;	When chronic pain persists for a prolonged period, the patient should use herbs and pills known as "cough drops," as well as applications of heat and cold and compresses.
et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	and if one performs the cauterization we have previously mentioned, it will not be effective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit;	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution and not too cold.
adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	then cauterize it deeply, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»;	After that, cauterize each corner of the shoulder bone, as we have said before, and cauterize the one called "vasselz" (vasculature).
et est I leus en coi on met ventouses;	and these are the veins where suction cups are placed.
et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os:	and hold your hand so that you do not see it touch the bone.
li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors;	the patient feels far greater pain from this cautery than from others, and I will speak of that later.
et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	and it is necessary that the cautery of the horns be more subtle than that of the middle part of the head, and this is its form.
dou cautere dou chief	For fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie:	When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and the disease spreads to the oil (or perhaps the brain), and the condition is purged with medicated treatments, and all other remedies as I have described in the division of diseases are tried, but they do not help.
adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	Then he performs cauterization according to two manners, that is to say, with hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir;	If he cauterizes with hot medicine, it is when you press a blistered area and remove the skin down to the flesh in small pieces, and then make an incision where the pain is located in such a way that you can replace the blister under the skin.
et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres;	and when it is replaced, if he tightens it well and leaves it thus for twelve hours;
et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III;	and then untie it and treat with sweet garlic, leaving the wound for two or three days.
puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	then place cotton soaked in butter over the wound until the pus stops.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	After the dressing, as long as it is clean;
et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	and if you see that any of the burning medicines I have written about or the dosages for treating with burning medicines are unsuitable, then adjust them as necessary.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery is done according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery with this tool:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance;	And it is called "closed" because the head is shaped like a clamp where there is a little curve, and it has a small appearance.
et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse;	and place it on the painful joint, hold your hand and gently twist it until half of the pain is gone.
et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	and release your hand when the artery is no longer blocked, it is healed, and there is abundant blood flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors;	After applying a bandage of twine, place it on the joint for three days;
puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez;	then I apply moist cotton in butter, and then treat the wound on the shoulder until it is healed;
et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare" (scalpel), be careful not to cut into the artery in this migraine that is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans;	When you treat a migraine as we have previously mentioned in the divisions of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery mentioned above is inadequate for the medicine and does not help, then you must heat up the cautery called "cultellare" (scalpel) until it is white.
et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os;	and thus mark the afflicted joint with a line half as long as a finger, and with one hand make an incision, pulling gently so that you do not touch the artery and do not go beyond the bone.
et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez;	guard the jaw that becomes mute when eating, and let the nerves pay no attention to anything but the muteness and lack of spasms in the patient, and be careful not to damage the blood flow from the artery once it is cut, as cutting it evokes great fear especially in those who do not know or have little experience.
et laisse l’uevre em mi voie;	and leave the wound half-healed;
mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	but I will tell you how to stop blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it clots in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee;	And if you see that this cautery is not enough to heal the disease, and the patient suffers, then cauterize both joints as we have said, and treat the wound until it is clean.
et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz;	and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter about the extraction of the artery, with a cautery having two blades.
et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	and this is the best cautery of them all and most helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	regarding the pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear due to cold, and various solvential medicines and other treatments as we have mentioned in the previous section have been applied, but the pain persists, use this cautery called "point," which has the following shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche;	After marking around the painful ear or both ears where pain persists, move slightly upwards from the root of the ear, then mark the place where the joint is.
et ait X poins entor chescune oreille;	and make X marks around each ear;
aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	after healing the joint, ensure it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	regarding the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie;	The torture that must be cured by cautery is limited to those that move with fluid, as we have said in the sections about disease.
et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	and do not perform cautery on appearances that come from dryness and spasms of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres:	When you cure this appearance of torture that moves with fluid from dryness and purging from the head and gargling, then it is not effective. Therefore, you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries.
l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres;	one at the root of the ear, another slightly below the temple, and the third in the adjustment of the two lips.
et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce;	and place the cautery on the part that opens a healthy wound, and make two cauterizations at the top of the ear, one slightly below the edge of the bone at the top, and another in the temple just as far away;
et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse;	and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned;
et c’est li forme dou cautere:	and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros;	and it resembles the knife we have placed in front, but it is a little more subtle, and it is necessary that the knife be slightly thicker.
aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing, the limb as I have said before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres:	When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said before, but the patient does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations:
II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac;	On the two horns of the head, I bind the head, and I open the limb called "vassel" as we have said before, and do no cauterization on the opening of the stomach.
et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	and let them be treated as we have said above.
de litargie	It seems like there might be a slight error or missing context
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil;	For this disease, it is necessary to give the patient large doses of herbs that purify the mind.
aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres;	after examining the patient's entire head, place the plaster of mustard on the occiput as described in the treatise on plasters.
et c’est li maniere dou cautere:	and this is the method of cauterization:
si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	if you do as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est;	If it is healthy thus, it is good.
et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros;	and if it is not, perform three cauterizations with hot iron on the thigh down to the collarbone, and leave two large spaces between each cauterization.
et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu;	and treat it as the others, and if you see it tighten, and the patient suffers, perform a cauterization in the middle.
et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it is necessary, two others on the two horns, and treat as long as it is healthy.
et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	and let the cautery be called "olive", as I have previously said.
de la froidor dou chief	from the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit;	The head should be cleansed with earth and water, as we have previously said.
aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col;	after cleansing the head with the patient's malady, then apply the cautery to the head and each horn, and behind, and three times on the spine of the column.
et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos;	and if you need more skill, and the body is moist and the patient suffers greatly, and the illness is severe, then apply four cauteries on the spine of the back.
et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main;	and let them grow until they are as long as possible, and gentle on the touch;
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	after the cure while it is healed, and perform the cautery that is called "olive" which we have previously mentioned.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use fire cautery unless they are phlegmatic; first, the brain must be purified with years and other treatments that we have discussed in the section on great suffering from prolonged medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes;	And if it is a young child who cannot endure it, make them gargle and chew, often cleansing the brain with good meat.
aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne;	after the king has placed his head in the middle, perform the cautery as we have said before, and cauterize the veins, and on each horn.
et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and if the patient is far and suffers, perform cautery on them as I have said to those with paralysis and softening of the flesh, on the spine of the back and neck, and cauterize them with olive oil according to the manner I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is ill, perform a delicate cautery on them according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, due to melancholy, excessive or corrupt moisture and thick fluid are present, then perform cautery with hot iron as we have described for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, due to melancholy, the excessive moisture declines into melancholia and the body of the patient is moist, then give them something to drink that purifies the mind, as described in the previous section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide;	After removing the head of the patient;
aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief;	after making the torus of the well-made bandage, just as I have described, place it on the head;
et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars;	and the patient should be crossed and held firmly from all sides;
aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien;	After applying this treatment, take some butter from an old goat;
et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir;	and heat it gently over fire, so that it does not burn the patient;
aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier;	after evacuating the ring from inside out near the base, and leaving it to cool down;
et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and do this to the patient once each week with another good remedy, as long as he is healthy.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you need to cauterize, make several incisions throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument;	This method of cautery moistens the brain increasingly;
et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	and then place a moist cotton wick in butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the eyes come first as signs of the conditions I described in the previous section, then begin and give to the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and guards against all moisture, and promotes sweating or a bath while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I;	Afterward, he commands the patient to raise their head, and applies heat to the head, performing two cauterizations on both temples if the headache descends from the brain, or on either side if it descends from one eye.
et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple;	and seal all the veins and arteries that are beneath the heart, making the cauterization long according to the width of the temple.
et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	and guard against the discharge of blood, and if you see too much blood issuing, stop it by applying pressure as you have learned.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras;	And I will teach you, in the extraction of arteries and the cauterization of incisions, how to stop it.
et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	and never cauterize or burn the skin between the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	two parts of the eye
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors;	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, cut the arteries that are visible just beneath the surface.
et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz:	and we see that these are cold, phlegmatic superfluities, so he applies the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of this chapter to them:
I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os;	I apply the cautery to the head, and I cauterize both temples, and I cauterize where the two bones join.
et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	and if it requires more, he cauterizes the eyelid carefully with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Let the body shed tears from its eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies;	When you medicate it according to what we have said in the previous discussion, and it does not benefit, then give the patient three bitter herbs to drink.
aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire;	After the king has taken the lead, and he performs the cauterization with olive oil as a mild cautery.
et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous;	and performs cauterization with the "claw" cautery on the shoulders, slightly pulling the hairs.
et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	and beware of the artery, do not block it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	This is the form of cauterization called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil becomes soft due to illness and moisture, then apply this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	Due to which the shape is:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont;	and if you see that the cauterizations on both shoulders are as long as the hairs on them,
et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	and do not let go of the hand until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the hair that does not allow the oil to pass through
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres:	It never happens that the hair of the veins is turned to darkness, and they prick the vein, and cautery is performed according to two manners:
c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	that is to say, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals;	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even;
et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain;	When they grow and are even, then place the patient in a healthy state;
aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz;	after signing on the paper of the eyes a figure that is as full of wonder, and it begins with the signs of the hairs.
puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	then dip cotton in moist glaze of egg and musk from rose, then heat the cautery with which the shape is as follows:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit;	After cauterizing the affected area little by little, ensure the colors are burnt into the skin deeply.
et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil;	and the signs of the work's effectiveness are that you see the skin retracting and the hairs standing on end at the touch of oil.
adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee;	then take your hand away and leave it thus for three days, then apply moist cotton coated in butter until the burning is gone.
aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	after the treatment, as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers;	And after this come the hairs, and the paper is softened, then begin again the cautery on that same place, as you did before.
et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if the hairs are burnt away, cauterize while the paper (skin) is raised to its natural state and even, and do not let the hairs prick the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte;	The medicinal burning cautery is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment shape of the leaf of myrtle.
puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien;	then take French soap and fresh charcoal, each one .5., and grind them together well;
et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz;	and apply it gently, if it does not cool down, then with a light touch on the shape you have made as if from a leaf, and place some paper on top of it.
et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi;	and if the disease persists only in one place, then surgery should be performed there, and also in both places.
et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef;	and apply oil of cotton moistened with egg on it.
et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	and the patient's joint should be in your healthy hand and place your finger over the medicine, and press lightly and move it every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for it burns just like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your body.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision;	And when the burning sensation has passed, if you raise the limb from below, and see that the paper is raised as if it were raised by constraint of fire or by incision.
et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point;	If no, then apply more of the medicine to the limb or the medicine has not opened up yet, as long as your work is even and your joints are set correctly.
puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a piece of moistened butter on it until the burning heat is extinguished, and afterward, treat the wound with the ointment called "dyafenis" or other remedies, as long as it remains clean.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if it is necessary for you, guard yourself well with your work, taking great care that it does not neglect the medicine at all.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant;	And if the paper becomes soft afterward and the hairs poke in the oil, then repeat the treatment on that wound which has been softened with the paper, just as you did before.
aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	afterward, treat it as long as it remains clean;
et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	and this is the form of the wound with great pain;
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens;	And know that the bones of men are diverse in size and shape, and according to these constraints...
et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	and do not depart from the right way for those who have the study of this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the sections on diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you should cauterize it according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain;	Instruct the patient to place his head in a healthy position.
et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief;	and hold the patient's head between your hands in this manner so that it does not move, nor do they wiggle their head.
aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil;	after moistening a cotton ball with hot or pepper juice on oil;
aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz:	after heating the cautery instrument that is half:
et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere;	and it should be shaped like the head of a quill, assembling the edge to form the cautery;
se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente;	if you look, it is pointed from one end to the other, and if you look, it is also like a tent;
mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	but nevertheless, this being bald is worth moving for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche;	After pressing the fistula, if it is open, drain the pus and dry it;

dou movement des dens	no movement of the joints

de la dolor des dens	from the pain of teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres:	When tooth pain arises due to cold or frost, and medical remedies are ineffective, then cautery should be applied according to these two methods:
et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	and with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain;	The butter cautery is such that you melt butter with heat, and apply it with the tip of a iron or silver spoon.

Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide;	He performs fire cauterization by applying it in such a way that you press a piece of iron or steel into the patient's flesh, making it thick enough to prevent the heat from reaching the surface of the wound.
