et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer;	and if the wound does not heal under your care, grind vitriol until it is well soaked, then return to your task until you have treated everything thoroughly.
puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then raise the limb from rest and from weight, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	No matter how often holes appear in the throat, which are called "godath", and we properly call them "two amandres", when you treat them, as we have said in the previous section, and they remain unsanitized, be careful.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	if they are small abscesses with a hard, pale surface, do not try to pierce them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red with a thick root, do not pierce it with iron, also because of the discharge of pus.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	but let it grow as long as it is strong, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	and if it is of a white color and the roots are subtle, then prepare the instrument to extract it, but first ensure that the abscess is calm and at rest.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme;	Then make the patient face the sun, and ensure their bowels are in good health. Open the mouth and press the jaws between their hands, pressing the tongue down with the instrument to form this shape.
et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and it should be of silver or fine gold, just like our knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues;	You cannot press the tongue against all these instruments and see the abscess, so take the needle and drive it into the sore, and pull it out from above as much as you can.
et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces;	and do not pull anything from the wound with it, then cut with the instrument, which forms something that looks like strength.
et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	but nevertheless, the head is bent, one way or another, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, if you make it with pliers, like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom;	And make incisions on one side, and on the other leave them untouched;
et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and when you have treated one of the abscesses, treat the other in the same way, and afterwards gargle the patient with hot water and clean, cool water, and the discharge of pus will occur, if the patient is gargled with hot water, or with cooked pomegranate skins, or myrtle leaves, or similar things, until the pus is cleared.
puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure it while it is still healthy;
et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And never does another abscess form in the throat other than the two glands, so bind them as tightly as the two glands.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens;	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was newly formed inside her throat, namely the small abscess.
et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	and had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, and could not eat or drink, and would have died if left thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two ribs through the two openings in the throat where it entered.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe;	I hasten to do so, and insert one pin, then pull it forcibly, and take a large portion of the bowel.
puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue;	then I repeat the process on the other side of the opening, and open the mouth and press the tongue.
aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc;	after inserting the pin into these abscesses, and taking out a portion, I pull only a little bit of blood.
et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens;	and thus the throat of the woman is opened, and she begins to drink water and then wine, and does not stop cutting into that abscess for a long time.
et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros;	and it (the abscess) repeatedly reopens, filling up again the space that I had emptied out, as long as it is very large.
adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge:	then I secured it and cauterized (the wound) inside the throat.
ensi demora sens croistre;	so it delays without growth.
et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	and I separated these parts, and let God do His work after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»;	When the eye returns to its socket, and it is swollen and distant, it is called "perpendicular".
et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	and if it is so large and round, then it is called a "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes;	When it is treated as we have described in the previous section, but the treatment does not help, and you notice that the abscess has subsided, and it appears subtle, then it is necessary to drain it.
et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe;	and the one that is round and compact, not distant.
et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	and it is red or of a dark color, then it is necessary to carefully perform the incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the sick person.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant;	It is necessary, when you see this, according to the manner I have said, of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument we spoke of earlier.
puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	then insert the hook into the eye and pull it out, and cut it with one of the instruments I mentioned in incising the two mandrils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil;	And it is necessary that you do not cut off more than the excess beyond the natural limit.
car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle;	for if you continue doing this, it will grieve your voice and words.
et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and after the incision, use what we have said about incising the two mandles, and heal it as long as it is clean.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient feels great pain, it is necessary that you use an instrument for cauterizing the sensitive parts.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The method of cauterization is very acute.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere;	And it is that the patient places his head on a healthy surface, and then presses his tongue with the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and immerses it in hot water, not too thick or too clear.
et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	and with the use of this instrument, which gives it the following shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve;	And let the physician have a comb, as if it were a spoon's handle, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the wound.
et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece;	and have the patient lying on their side, so that saliva and mucus from their mouth can drain the medicine without going down to the throat, and thus healing.
puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie;	then take your hand and press the medicine onto the wound for about half an hour, until you see it cease to hurt and the pain from the medicine subsides.
et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve;	and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all the way into the hole in the cotton, until the cotton is saturated with the liquid.
et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V.	and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and remove after three or four days.
Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine;	And if you need to repeat the cauterization with the medicine, when repeating it, after cauterizing, wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean everything around the medicine.
et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	and he should be raised with cold water, and he should be cured with gargles until he is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere;	This treatment is safer than incision, rather than cauterization.
s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir;	if it is treated with fumigation according to this method, take cayenne pepper and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and similar herbs, and combine all of them or any of them in a pot, and add water, and boil.
et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	and the pot should be tightly sealed with strong clay, and on top of the pot, use a lid according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie;	And whether it is of silver or gold, and if one of the joints is closed in the mouth of the patient, so that the vapour rises to the eye through the chain, until the eye becomes numb.
aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent;	after the recurrence often, while the eye dries and heals, be sure not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, as many complications arise.
et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	and do not make any movements except during the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut;	And if this instrument is not available, take a chain and put a piece of cloth in the mouth of the patient, so that it is not too hot.
car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	because the heat of fire does not allow moisture to accumulate in the mouth, and this is a good remedy for overall health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose;	often there is a burning sensation in the throat from bone or fish spine, or any such thing;
si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose;	so it is necessary that you treat what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the tool, so that you may observe the thing move.
et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac;	and if it does not open and is swallowed into the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit so that the food may be cooked in the stomach.
par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement;	by chance if this thing turns around through vomiting;
ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec;	or the patients swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of cucumber, or a lettuce root, or a dry crust of bread;
et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse;	and hold the sponge in its mouth and then swallow it;
et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer;	and when it arrives at the stomach, if it is hard, then pull it out forcefully;
et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not come from what we have said, take a plunger tool according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit;	and let the instrument be curved towards the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and hold the head slightly raised.
et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens;	and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, so that nothing comes out, and do not push the bone inside.
et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse;	and it is important that the patient pushes the instrument, because if he does not move it, the object inside will be stuck.
si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	if the bottle sinks, pull it out with all the tools equally, until it is completely empty.
de la sansue de la gorge	regarding the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines;	No treatment should be administered without considering the symptoms, as I mentioned in the previous section, through the use of medicines.
et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	and if it does not help, then look into the throat of the patient with the sun, and press their tongue with the tool I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it out with all its small pins, or subtle pliers that are fit for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a sheep's gut, insert it into the throat of the patient with the disease, then twist or lift the gut in hot water and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient suffers from fever all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent;	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it into both cheeks, moving it with your hand frequently.
et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	and if at any time he feels pain, then it is certain.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve;	And if it does not give way as we have said, then the patient should be treated with the instrument used in the fumigation of the eye with ash, to dislodge the foreign body.
fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	do this many times, for it will come out without resistance.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument;	The method of fumigation is as follows: you take a pot with a hole in the middle, lined with a perforated cover, and place the instrument to be fumigated inside.
puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue;	then pour the smoke treatment, and have the patient put the tip of the cane in their mouth and close it tightly, so that no smoke escapes, but it comes up to the throat.
et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois;	and the blood will now flow, and if it does not come out, repeat the smoke treatment many times.
et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue;	and the patient suffers from thirst, and chews salty and sour things, but does not drink water.
et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	and then it will be easier for her to speak without this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge;	And the shape of the instrument with which one treats the wound, if it can be seen, resembles twisted pliers designed to enter the throat.
et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier;	and it resembles the beak of a bird of prey, and has the roughness of limestone, so that whatever it grasps, it cannot let go.
et vez ci la forme:	and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Many appearances of abscesses are, according to the memory that comes to mind after reading this book, and they differ in penetration and size.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	and this is through two manners, one being just like its own image, and of those that are held by moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the joints where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess on the upper part of the body is different from that at its base, and the abscess of the fleshy parts of the limb is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if there is no need to pierce an abscess, as long as the bowel remains dead according to its completion;
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if they are such that it is necessary to pierce when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, like abscesses which are in healthy joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from damaged joints, and it is left until it becomes gangrenous around, perhaps the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Or, the abscess is in the main member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	if he has a wound in the fundament, pierce it in such a way that it becomes dead.
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	and it is not advisable that you pierce an abscess without completing the healing process, otherwise, if he has a wound in the fundament, it will not heal completely and become fistulated.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and it will not heal fully in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes;	And it is important that you know the right time for piercing an abscess when it is dead, according to its completion, and this is when the pain is soothed, and the fever leaves, and the swelling diminishes in the affected area, and the abscess becomes smooth and well-shaped, and other signs appear.
et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues;	and it is necessary that you make the piercing sit more dependent on the abscess, where it opens movement.
et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	and the piercing should be as long as the body, and if the abscess is in the hand or foot, or in the joints and tendons and arteries, and everywhere it is even without any curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when there are abscesses in the fatty parts of the body, it is better to leave the incision until the swelling has subsided after the digestive process, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure;	For if you pierce it in front of this one, the body's veins will be stretched from the pressure, and it will be filled with much filth.
et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	and by chance they harden the lips and deepen the wound within him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that is pierced according to the thickness of the body, as needed by the member.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus;	and it is necessary that you heal small wounds, small openings;
et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme;	and in large wounds, large openings, and many cracks according to the size of the wound;
et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper;	and if for such wounds it is necessary to pull the heart, and cover;
quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes:	when it becomes as dry as cloth and is numbed, then it must be treated as we do with blisters.
et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres;	and if they are split in three angles, or such as we cut like the fur of myrtle, or abscesses from attacks;
et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	and if it is such that we make a deep cut, and other sizes and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;	Those that have no head, like a soft, superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce them deeply.
et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie;	and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has a strong bow, and you pierce it, if you cannot draw out all the bow in that moment, but only part of it.
puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief;	then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out something from it;
fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute;	do this many times with great effort, until the bow completely draws out;
meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	most often the patients are of weak constitution, or pregnant women, or very young children, or old, frail people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For often the patient jumps with fear at the sound of the bow, which may cause the sick to die, and you will not be blamed.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite;	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, if the wound is cleaned, and observe whether the wound of the abscess is small.
et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton;	and if it is a deep wound, then apply linen or fresh cotton.
et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre;	and if it is a large abscess with many openings, then you should insert a tent into each one so that they come together.
et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor;	and if you have a portion of hard skin in the abscess and it is closed around it, then you should fill it with dry cotton or linen raspings without moisture and bind it for three days.
puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the bone, and the treatment of the wound until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood flow occurs due to the operation, apply cold water and ice, and moisten the compress, and place it over the bleeding joint repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut;	And if the blood poisoning persists, with appropriate governance and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the eyes or the abscesses are very sensitive, then you must place these and cover them with moist cloths of wine and hot oil.
et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit;	and if it is in summer and the eye is fleshy, then you must place moist cloths of water and oil, or wine and fresh oil, for three days, as we have said.
et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then remove the abscess and clean it and treat it as appropriate while it is still fresh.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes:	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses:
or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	or as told to you, how one should proceed before the treatment of abscesses, read this chapter now.
des soros	from sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or sometimes the chief sickness comes from small abscesses, and they are like threads, also like the sinew of a goose, and there are many similar ones.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz;	There are some that are large and soft, as well as those with moisture also containing pulsations;
et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	and if it is of such as are hard and resistant to cutting, and there is no doubt that the arteries do not act against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the trunk is such that you should try all instruments called "intrusive", from which the shape below comes, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they make a hole from above down long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien;	And when the moisture is evacuated, if scraping leaves no skin containing the moisture, for it repeatedly returns when nothing is left.
puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens;	then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present;
se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor;	if not, with water and string, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day;
et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	and they will correct what is delayed from moving.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit;	And then begin the treatment again, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are sure that it does not delay from moving.
puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then dress the wound with suitable medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc;	And if the abscess persists for a long time, following this form, then cut it deeply.
et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist;	and he should soak the wounds, scrape them from all sides, and use all your care to draw out the pus from the wound where it lies.
et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	and if the arteries react against it, do as I have told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do the same for an abscess that is persistent and hard, cutting and treating it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And make an incision above the abscess and around it, if it is softer, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme;	And if none of these abscesses or joints have any moisture, and it is one of these deep abscesses that I incised on an old woman's shoulder;
et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier;	and I found the abscess as hard as a sharp, white stone that cannot be broken.
et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	and if none of these helps, one would also make a wound as deep as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe;	In other cases, when the pain comes in the upper parts, such as the top of the head and the roots of the ears, keep the opening closed for several days so that the bowels can move.
et les cure si com il covient.	and treat it as appropriate.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times this abscess appears in the neck, and dissolves the adhesions, and attacks the angles, and never occurs elsewhere on the body, and it is painful, and twisted upon itself.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit;	And each ulcer is properly inside its bone, just as the sore and abscess on the head, as we have said before.
et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some of them contain moisture, and there are others that are malicious and refuse to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde;	in that case, when you see a good disposition for touch, and it resembles the healthy color of the skin, and is quiet from every side, and not rigid at the joint nor in the tendon, or too deep.
si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief;	you must then lift it from above, and peel the skin from every part, and the two lips of the heart should be at once, if necessary, as we have said in the chapter of the head.
et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	And move it little by little, and be sure not to touch the nerve or the vein, nor be too aggressive with the knife, so that your hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, lest you miss what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie;	And if you hit the vein or artery and it does not allow you to work, apply vitriol or any powder that stops blood flow, and close the wound.
et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	and leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound becomes softer, and begins to heal.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses;	And when the wound is stained with blood, it returns to your work, as long as you complete it.
puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	then seek your finger's subtle indications if there remain no small lumps, if it scrapes and cleans.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement;	And if there is a large vein in the root of the lump, it is not enough that you only scrape off this lump at its root, but tie a double strand of thread around it and leave it hanging without harm.
puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	then apply the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then dress it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut off the entire sore, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, so that there is no delay due to the size of the sore.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you need to understand how to deal with the root of the issue, pull it out forcefully, and cut it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure;	Those scrofulas that hold an excess, cut them where they appear to be closing;
et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption;	and make the cut in the same way as that mentioned above, depending on the case, then apply these remedies and similar things, so that it corrupts those who are stuck in the corruption.
et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when the wound is well cleaned, if the healing remedy causes pain, as long as it heals.
de squinance	squinance (n.) - squint or cross-
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge;	The ancients spoke and wrote about the treatment of the throat.
mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	but I have never seen it done in our land, and it is the writing of their word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee;	For those with a squint, it is necessary that the fold in the throat, called the epiglottis, be avoided.
et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	and no help is done through this, because all the veins and the pores of the sick person are close in those who have an abscess in the mouth, or throat, or intestines.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the channel of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to divide the epiglottis, we should do so in three or four small cuts across, between the two circles, or according to the depth of the cut, not into the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if these muscles are suitable for cutting the epiglottis, then there is no risk, and the vessels are long and thin.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary to stretch the throat skin to its fullest extent, and cut the heart open until it reaches the chest.
et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	and avoid the blood vessels, if you see anything, and then cut the syphilis as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated through the cutting of the chest's blood vessel that bursts from the place which is broken, and by the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige;	And when the hour has passed and there is doubt about the strangulation, gather the two edges of the wound together with care, and cut through them all the way to the cartilage.
puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then administer medications that induce warmth, as long as they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasim understands that one must not proceed until the throat is completely sealed, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, lacking all hope.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot strain, and they will breathe through the wound, thus preventing death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	and for this, the ancients command to keep the wound open until the evil of the disease has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat, as long as it was healed.
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and stabbed it into her throat, and cut part of the tongue from the gums.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that was coming from it; I realized that there was no proper vein or channel leading to the throat, but the veins were emerging from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was clean;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and having restored the damsel's voice, which had been hoarse, she returned to her previous state.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	because I say that there should be no fear in the operation of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Cysts in the throat are called "neck hernias", and they are large apertures colored like an arrow, and they are common in women;
et est selonc II manieres:	and this is according to two manners:
naturez, et accidens;	natural and accidental;
ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	in nature, there is no mechanism.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	and the accidental is according to two manners: one is similar to a tumor, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that arises from an artery.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and it causes fear, and one should not attempt to make fire outside in a large place; rather, they should test and examine the entry point carefully.
se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	If you let it grow out as much as a new grass, and it does not give way to any force, if it is broken, just as we break our bones, and treat it with all your care, if there is no pain.
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and wrap it tightly, and treat it as appropriate, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	From us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	There are many ways of which I will describe all their similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	and it is necessary that I explain all the differences between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture;	I say that the origin is heat and fever holding, as long as the ebullition has not passed, and completion of the putrefaction.
adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	then rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new heat, there is neither fever nor pain, and it contains satisfaction, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a wound, and becomes swollen.
et sont selonc II semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and they are according to their appearances, whether oily, moist, or of a certain color, as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You should, when you come to the treatment of a new patient, first try and inquire about all the instruments called "entromissory", according to their form, as described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of questioning abscesses is that you press more moistly where you feel the abscess, and move your fingers little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the center, according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	then extract the instrument, and be careful of any sudden jumps.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture is running through the flesh, what color it has, do as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if moisture does not come from the instrument, know that it is full, then do crosswise and take it as tongs, scraping gently from each side and taking care of the cloth where it lies so you draw out the pus with the new.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if nothing remains, it will return to the body many times.
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if a small amount remains and does not disturb you, apply some corrosive powders or hot compresses to the wound, treat it with cooling things, and use other remedies until it is healed.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if the wound is large, cut both edges of the wound and treat it with remedies to promote healing.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc;	and if the pain is intense or persistent, apply a poultice of crushed vitriol and leave it for two or three days, until the wound heals and the blood flow subsides.
puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	then return to covering what has been dislocated from the new.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres:	See the shapes of the instruments used for dislocation, which are of three types:
grans et moien et petit;	large, medium, and small;
et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres:	and then take three squares that are called "albaret," and one that is called "breb," and there are three ways to do this:
grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	cut, fine, and small, to encircle the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and are also like needles used to cut sorceries, made of gold, or iron, or silver, and the ones that are yellow in color are more effective for encircling the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the opening's size.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci:	The shapes of the incisions are much alike, as you can see here:
grans, moiens, et petis;	great, medium, and small;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi;	and if the incisions have two curves in three ways as well;
et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres;	and if they are once which have three curves, and are also of three manners;
et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres;	and if they are once which have two curves, and once only one curve, and are of three manners;
et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and all this is necessary for their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these [instruments] must be sharp, and there are some that do not cut well from both sides, which scrape the skin, so that one does not cut into the vein or nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	and from these intrusions, the splinters are removed from many parts, so that the patient does not lose them when opening the abscesses.
et sont de III manieres:	and they are of three kinds:
grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	great, small, and medium, as you see.
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and do not use any more force than necessary, especially with fleshy parts like legs, arms, mammary glands, and similar areas.
et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	and never use any other small instrument resembling the edges of fingers, according to this form, to stop blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it should never be placed in a place that severs veins and arteries, and never according to this great form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	never inflame the breasts of any man when they begin to be corrupted, as long as they appear like a woman's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	and become pale and swollen, and anyone who wants to cure them should do so according to this form from this line b until g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then scrape off the fat, and apply medicinal fire to the wound, then bring together the two edges of the wound with stitches, and heal it as long as it is clean.
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures;	and it holds the eye downward, and is loosened by its size, as happens with women, when they give birth in two places, through two similar openings.
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	so that one holds the other at the end of each, and the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line. b. to the next line. g.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then strip the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have mentioned about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary for treatment, as long as it is healthy.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if he is not healthy, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to blood flow, it is necessary that you fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive dressing.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	and leave it until it absorbs the moisture and fat, then dress it as long as it remains healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	from the abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	Abscesses that come from beneath the armpits are hard scrofulous nodules or they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus in the abscess is drained, apply clean cotton to the wound and leave it for another day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with suitable medicine until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then it should be treated as we have said about the cuts in scrofula, and if the wound gapes, then apply cautery as we have previously stated.
de la routure de l’artere	from the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is blocked and the skin above it is sealed, many abscesses form, and this also occurs in the vein with an inflammation and abscess.
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if you recognize it thus when it is for the artery, then cut deep enough to reach the abscess;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement;	and when you feel it with your hands, if it feels strange;
et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when it is for the vein, then there should be a strong appearance of redness;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	and it is madness to cover this abscess, especially when it is deep in the flesh and filled with anger and other substances, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	It is necessary to avoid iron cure, and he who has the main problem should also be cautious, and in the case of an artery exposed through the skin, make a long cut above it.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	then open the wound in small incisions, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues, while it is exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples;	then insert a needle from the inside and pierce it to the other side, gripping the artery with a double thread in two parts, according to what I have taught you regarding the extraction of both arteries located in the temple.
puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	then mark the place between the two joints of an instrument as long as there is no pain from it, and release the abscess.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	then administer the treatment as needed, as long as the ligaments remain strong.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then apply this treatment as long as it is healthy.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	and if the abscess is as large as a vein, it is necessary that you hold in your hand what you can reach of the abscess all around, then insert the needle through the skin and pierce it, and pass the thread double, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil;	then, as I have told you, take the abscess, or one of the parts of the thread to the shoulder;
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus;	and if you doubt that the thread is not strong enough, if it rebounds another needle through all the abscess, from the base to the incision of the first needle, and pulls the threads in four directions;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut the abscess until the excess is gone, then cut off the excess with a cure, and leave what is tied.
puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place a damp cloth of wine and oil on it, and administer treatments with bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	from the abscess of the nail
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly to how abscesses occur in arteries and veins, nails can also develop abscesses when they are injured or subjected to excessive work, among other things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	And this occurs more often with dislocations and joints in all parts where there are articulations, and it is a sharp abscess, and its appearance resembles the colour of the flesh, and it is in various positions causing pain.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when they tighten it, the patient feels pain, and is not completely healed of the injury, but the heart remains weak.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer:	and it must be completely still from all sides, and does not move forward or backward, neither down nor up, and the one in joints should not be covered with metal.
par aventure i vanroit contraction;	perhaps they have a spasm;
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	and those who have a head or forehead, make the skin smooth with the scalpel.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	if the abscess is small, use tweezers to grasp it and cut it at its base;
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it is large, suspend it with a hook, and scrape off the skin, then cut through the bone and sew up the wound until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	The phrase "des grosses boces pendans" translates roughly to "hanging large
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros;	No such thing occurs in bellies or anywhere else, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its appearance, and it has subtle roots, and large excrements.
et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	and it has both small and large ones.
et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I have seen at home those who had them in the belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, had a fine root, were well-split, and always secreted moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I gathered them and found one weighing XVIII ounces, and another VI З., and the work of the incision is such that if you look at the patient, their moisture is evident, and the color of the articular surface is white and moist with a delicate root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	if you remove them with a broad spatula, they should be in your presence for fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	For cutting often brings great danger of blood loss, and if without your notice, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors;	and if you see the patient afraid and fearful of the incision to be made, take a well-prepared thread, and with it tie the wound as we have said, and leave it for a day.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail;	then restrain them, and do not cease to tighten the thread until it pulls the wound closed without effort.
et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne;	and if the roots are thick, be afraid to close them especially for the belly, but you can well close half of them, then cauterize it so that it does not reopen.
puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	then treat the wound, and ensure you do not cover the part that is red, pale, and lacks sensation and milk-white.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess enhanced, and I will come to the treatment of cancer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the wound is closed due to crusting.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the bump is due to cautery or an opening in a syphilis wound, and it is on the belly and not in any of the bowels, as is the case with other ruptures, or pus that drains from veins or arteries according to what is above, or from flatulence;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	and if it is from the rupture of syphilis and the discharge from the bowels, then the abscess has a color similar to that of the skin, and it causes little pain, and opens up with various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to an intestinal issue, then it is more complex, and when pressed at the patient's will, it rebounds, and sometimes becomes tightened, greatly constricting the entry to the bath and causing much effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie;	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and it opens well when you press it with your hand, it does not constrain.
et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	and if it is due to blood, it opens up through these signs: the abscess is large and hard, and it is fixed in place according to its quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to wind (or gas), it feels soft upon touching, and the work required is such that you must observe whether its appearance indicates blood from an artery, a vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary, you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter about abscesses, both for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowels, then you must instruct the patient to keep quiet and lie entirely still, and then tie a cloth around the entire area.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	then command the patient to gently move it between their hands, then enter the area you have marked with a cloth, and stretch half of the abscess above all the sharp edges.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	then tie it with a strong thread or a firm cord of strong silk, and make sure the knot is tight.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	then open half of the abscess extended over the bandage, and press your index finger into it, seeking the inner organs.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	if you feel it grip the ligament, release it, and press the intestine out through the opening in the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the swelling, take it at the point, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the artery or vein runs counter to your work, then return to your task and take two needles, press them firmly, and push both needles back in the same way you made the incision.
puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	then stretch the abscess in four directions over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, leaving the place to heal, and seek death by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	where it is tender and possible, then treat it as appropriate, and heal the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the place as appropriate, and bind the wound.
dou chancre	A cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have spoken in the previous section about the signs of an abscess, and how it must be treated with medicine, and how one should avoid iron treatment.
et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement;	And let us speak of the ulcer that invades the wound, and take great care in its cure, and say to the ancients that when an ulcer is present or can be cut out like an ulcer on the mammary gland, or the thigh, or similar places, then it must all be removed when it first appears.
et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner;	and when it is large and old, then you should not approach it, for I can never heal it.
ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	no one has ever healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire;	And for the work, when it is in place or can be removed, as we have said, it is that you repeatedly clean the patient of black bile.
puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige;	then make it healthier if there is visible improvement, then operate on the patient in a good place to perform the work.
puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier;	then pour onces or chancres, and wash all parts, and clean all parts without leaving any residue;
et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez;	and let the blood flow completely, and carefully press the place with your hand or any object, and if the bleeding continues after the treatment of the wound, cauterize it until the blood is stopped.
puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply other remedies as long as he is healthy.
de ydropisie	From hydropsie (a condition marked by excessive fluid accumulation
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer:	We have previously discussed the similarities of edema, and how the gathering of fluid is formed, the signs of each condition, and the treatments using medications, as well as those treated with iron.
si est eclites soulement;	if it is only slightly swollen;
et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances:	and one should not use iron for these two conditions:
c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;	This is to know, namely, tympanitis and impetigo, for it is a mortal thing.
donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses;	So then, when you treat this appearance of dropsy, which is called 'edema', and the cure does not benefit, consider if the patient is weak or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as intestinal ailments or similar conditions.
si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;	if they do not allow iron to touch them, for there is doubt.
et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	and if you see the patient with great strength and they have no other illness but dropsy alone, and they are neither too weak nor too strong, then thus should you proceed:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	Place the patient upright on your hands, and the minister presses the belly towards the end, pointing the water to the lowest part of the pain, then take the spiny spatula according to this form.
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And make incisions from the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	at the tip, but not so deeply that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot be broken.
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines:	then check if there is any inflammation towards the intestines:
si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil;	if it is necessary, you must cut through the bowel three times straight down from the top of the finger.
et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois;	and if the dislocation is due to a weak liver, it occurs on the left side of the hip three joints down.
et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	and if it is due to moisture, it occurs on the right side, and it is not appropriate for the patient to lie on the dislocated joint so that excess fluid does not flow to the weak liver.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor;	then cut through all the skin with the instrument, and press, and apply your hand to the entire area between the skin and the muscle just as if you were peeling it, in the quantity of a fingernail or around that area.
puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	then pierce the soft flesh until the knife reaches the bone, and it is the white of the wound, then pull out this instrument, and with it, form the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus;	and it resembles a thin silver chain, made of fine gold or silver, and in the middle part there is a small hole.
et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus;	and on one side, three holes.
et II d’autre part, et I d’autre;	and two on the other side, and one on yet another.
et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	and it is the shoulder cut as if with a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument;	at the top of it there is a wound, so that when the instrument comes into contact with water, it sinks straight down onto the instrument.
