Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes;	and if the mouth of the wound is tightly closed, we have said the remedy of sneezing and inhalation of herbal fumes.
et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire;	and if it is not from any of the things we have said, be careful not to follow a false lead.
mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is important that what is in the mouth of the wound, you bind to the woman's thigh, then cleanse it with a four-ingredient remedy.
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer;	if the bone goes out of place and is put back, it will come again.
mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but nevertheless, when it comes out so that there is a bad smell in the stomach and head, and the patient becomes sick.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu:	Therefore, it is necessary to use suitable fumigants:
aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	no one has tried the fumigation of parsley and dried figs before.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which the woman is fumigated to stop the flow of blood and the bleeding so is this one.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it resembles a tube, similar to a cane, and one places the head gently in the earth, and the wide end over the fire.
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let there be fumigations over the coals, and the scurvy until it is cured, and then another begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet had their foundations perceived; instead, they are wrapped in subtle cloth.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it is necessary in the bath that he perceives this subtlety at its proper place, and does not pierce it with a sharp object, and holds back the tightening so that it does not touch.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	then place it on a moist cloth soaked in wine and oil, then apply the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, insert a plug of wool or cloth, and leave it for several days, and when the child is strong enough to move around in rooms, then remove it.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme;	And at no time does this sudden stop of a wound or abscess occur.
si covient coper celui soudement:	if it is necessary to cover this sudden stop:
si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	if it is cured, as we have said about the pain of the wound.
de la fistule dou fondement	regarding the fistula from the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors;	Fistulas that originate from beneath the foundation are called nodosities, and those that come from above the foundation are larger, or in the space between the two parts, if there is a fistula or multiple fistulas.
et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans;	and when this node is old, if it opens again, and the moisture causes a white or subtle bow, and these fistules do not persist.
et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and they are known because of what arises from it or discharge when the patient has discharge, and by chance, one jumps up.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge;	And if the fistules pierce through to the bladder, and through to half of the penis;
et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	and reach up to the joint of the thigh, and up to the other part of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus recognize the present fistula in the fundament, and not elsewhere.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you insert your index finger or fundament, and push a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if there is curvature, if you insert a fine point or a horsehair, as long as you feel the tent or hair with your finger;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you do not feel it, and it does not come out through curvature or expulsion or pus, as we have said;
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie;	says that she does not feel any pain;
si te haste dou curer.	if you hurry with the cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or up to the urethra, if it lets go of the urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it is felt just at the joint of the thigh, then there is danger that the vein becomes blocked.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no twisting or sudden pain around it, and if it bends at all, then there is no need for sudden medication or dressing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and for these persistent fistulas, there is no sure cure but toil and the vain efforts of ignorant practitioners.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos;	In those that are neither persistent nor ancient, there is hope for healing by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands.
et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and holds the legs up to their thighs, with their thighs bent towards their belly;
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then apply a bandage of yarn, or cloth if there is flexibility, as long as you know where the bandage should go.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet;	If the patient feels pain deep within, it is necessary to insert your index finger, then they will feel that the pain is being pierced.
et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	and if you feel it exposed between your thumb and index finger, where the pain or discomfort is felt, then know that it is present.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if it cannot be treated with any effort, then it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One can nonetheless do everything one can to heal it, but this rarely happens.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and with this aid, it is necessary to apply a gentle cautery according to the size of the fistula, as mentioned above.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement;	and heat the entire area of the fistula until it removes the source of the problem;
et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and do this two or three times, as long as you know that these charred marks are healed, which resemble the quill of an eye;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then apply moist bandages made of butter until the charred marks are healed, and subsequently use a healing dressing that is hot and soothing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healthy, that's good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If this cannot otherwise be healed;
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if it attempts to enter, and does not pierce through the flesh or the foundation, and between your finger and the attempt, place a thick covering of cloth or something similar, and you will see the fistula through the covering where the warmth is.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	if you remove the cover from the beginning of the fistula and pull it back before attempting to treat it, and then apply heat afterwards, as long as it reaches the tip of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra;	and the tent will be delivered and removed.
puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	Then disfigure those bones that look like a bird's feather, and leave nothing intact.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pain strikes you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or sharp medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses:	For fire cautery joins two bones together:
c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	that is to say, the burning of these adjusted bones, and the inflammation of blood and the dryness of moisture;
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat the damp wounds with butter or ground herbs, as long as the bones are bowed, and push the burned bones back into their place.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat the wound with hot, hard, burning coals, and these are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	Because once it is restored, it becomes healthy and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula appears all the way to the bottom of the foundation and is removed from the body, if you press on its root or foundation, it hurts.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres:	If you feel the pulse, and it is between the pulse or the throbbing or the pain, and it is ready to pierce, if there is no other way of salvation and hope, through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it out completely, or if you can, apply tent and treat it first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not push too hard, so that you do not disturb the structure that holds the foundation, and let the eliminations happen on their own without force.
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then apply the cure, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	in case it turns out to be healthy, remove that covering and clean it, then apply pressure until it heals from the root, either with a bandage or another suitable instrument.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then remove all foreign bodies in the wound as much as possible;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement:	then study to restore the wound, and hold the fistula in check in the area where the foundation is lacking.
si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	if it is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere:	And never are fistulas like this:
et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	and it is when you press on the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation through the skin above, then take a needle sharp at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the wire crookedly inside, pushing the tent all along the fistula as far as it will go at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is persistent at the edge of the foundation inside, then pull the thread from that hole, so you secure your finger or foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II;	and take the thread from the joint, and bring together both parts, tighten one on the other, and leave it for one or two days.
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and do not loosen it, as long as the thread breaks through these three parts between them and moves.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then dress the wound as long as it is sealed and clean.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If you cannot pierce the fistula, no matter how much you try, it is not pierced deeply enough.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not appropriate to make the closure too tight, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	It is a form of sharp, spiky tissue from which one makes the fistula if it is very thick and hard, cutting through its parts.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand, for if one cannot do it, or should not do it, as you see here:
des emorroydes	Of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres:	There are two kinds of hemorrhoids:
ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement;	or they are inside the anus, resembling grains of resin, both small and large, and sometimes there is blood, and sometimes many, extending from the anus to the opening, deep into the anus or near its opening.
mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	but those that are too dry have little moisture, and still remain, or a bit of clear water or some blood, and have the colour of fresh flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those who have them deep within the foundation: so instruct the patient to stretch and move about in rooms, as long as the foundation remains firm, until the children are born.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you act quickly, and have a pince, or hold it with your finger, then cut it at the roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if they cannot hold them for their moisture, if they take them in the draping or cotton or a piece of chamoix;
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and extract them at their roots, then cut them and cover with any hot powders that are suitable for cauterizing;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery, and apply other remedies until they are healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot be removed, then wash the patient with a sharp and strong enema to clean what is in the foundation, so that it can come out easily;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	Let the patients take care, and if their pain is strong at the root, it is a light cure.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and if you press them with your thumb or pliers, cut them, then heal them as we have said, while they are healthy, and they fear the incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:	It is necessary that you administer the stitch according to this manner:
pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	take a thin thread, twist it into a needle, then pass the thread through from above and pierce the needle from below, and bring both ends of the thread back under the needle, making them wide.
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and holds the thread tight, then ties it off, extracts the needle, and does thus with all the others, leaving some to drain off the excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then places a moist cloth or oil-soaked compress on the affected area and commands the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and leaves it until it heals, and once fallen, applies curative treatments and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	Carefully and thoroughly from herbs or foundations
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is a drying up of herbs in the intestine, due to constraints of nature, and when the illness is old and no medicine avails.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you remove the skin with a scalpel or your finger, preventing it from moistening.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it as long as it is sound, as it should be;
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot be sound, then begin the razor again more strongly than before, as long as it is still moist, and it will be cut.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it as long as it is healed.
dou fremit	He trembles.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	a flea is a small, hairy appearance before the skin, and it goes into the flesh very deeply.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and never does the fire touch it, and he feels as if he is dying from trembling, and it spreads throughout the body, and there are more pains in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the cure is that you take a feather from an goose, or a strong feather from a falcon, and place that feather on the trembling, until the red circles cover the trembling entirely.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand over the entire feather until it covers all around the trembling, and press it firmly, and extract the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this of an iron or steel cable according to this form, and be subtle from below and draw from above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser.	I do not understand, for it makes me weak, and I must hold firm.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, if cauterization pricks, as it is in front or at the beginning of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a dish
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet;	Never use silver or gold enemas, or molten iron or brass wire.
et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	and never use these small and large instruments, according to those who are accustomed to them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	He who thus administers treatment to children and those who are weak and afflicted, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema is small and wide at the top, or the abdomen is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez;	and he should have a desire or the belly should be tied, as you see, and the feces should be perceived inside.
et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I;	and he has a hole on one side of the ribcage, and on the other side, one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and the belly or womb should be filled with medicines from a bladder of a beast or parchment, and perceived around all the small holes, and between each hole there should be a distance of space, then thread through these holes a strong thread made of twisted crisscrossed fiber in X or any other way, and tighten the abdomen as if it were a bowstring.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize;	and when the medicine is prepared, tie it to the instrument with a strong thread, then rinse.
et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it takes the form of a soft circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and apply a warm compress to the head with oil or egg yolk or similar, then wrap it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet;	then the healer should massage it with both hands together, until it is completely warm, then remove the compress and ask the patient to lean against the wall, lifting their legs slightly, allowing the medicine to exit as best it can.
et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if he sleeps soundly through the night, it is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you use the enema for a stomach disorder and the medicine quickly escapes, then it returns as soon as it is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant;	And if the hemorrhoid is at the foundation or an abscess, then the enema should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of the subtle enema where the skin is tightened:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	or we will tell you the treatments of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made of, and according to the place where the wounds are made, and from what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by the use of stone, and sword and knife, or spear or axe or arrow, or similar things;
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or according to the laws of the body, such as a wound that breaks through the skin, or the head, or the leg, or the belly, or the liver, and similar parts;
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and begin with simple head wounds, as the memory of their treatment will come in their chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut:	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it's due to a blow from a stone or similar things, and the skin is nonetheless torn and the wound is deep, and you slightly doubt an abscess forming.
si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	if it quickly becomes healthier from the cephalic wound, especially if there is little blood from the wound, and on the contrary, if the healing is in the affected part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and patients should avoid wine and rich meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if he does not want to get better, his flesh will waste away, and he should not drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and apply a poultice to the wound, if it is an abscess, then use cotton moistened only in rose oil or strict wine;
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, as long as it has fresh blood and is not moved by air or powder, I will say a little bit later.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if it burns him, as long as he does not put any bandages, he will be healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, such as the size of a sword or similar, and the edges cannot be brought together by tenting, then bring them together with stitching, as I will say about abdominal wounds, from the suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope;	If the wound is open, raw, and does not heal but only lasts for a short time, then it must be treated.
puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	then treat the wound with medicine and restore hard skin in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat hearty meats, such as beef and cooked wheat, as well as poultry and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find putrid flesh, not reaching the bone, and treat it immediately, cutting out all decay and applying a poultice.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which without cut, cannot be stopped by medications, if you wish to cut it, and if you dislocate it, hold it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere:	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light:
et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	and it is that you put this powder which hardens so that the fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est:	And the method of the powder is thus:
pren encens une partie;	take a portion of the incense
sanc de dragon II parties;	dragon's blood, two parts
chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	fresh salt, three parts, and mix the powder subtly, apply to the wound, and form it tightly, until it disperses well and joins all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle;	and then pack it well, and leave it to loosen, if it doesn't swell.
car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	because one cannot have medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never should charcoal be used alone if you do not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has not moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has moved the wound, especially if it is deep, unless someone puts this powder on it;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but apply no hot compresses or poultices made of ground oats mixed with water and honey while it is still fresh.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	then apply other remedies as long as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if a bone fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with delicate pincers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you after that about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the collar (or neck).
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound occurs on the collarbone and it is simple, with no distinction between it and any other part of the bone, but there is damage to the nerves or arteries in the collarbone.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, there is no other treatment but to let them heal, and put nothing restrictive, for it harms the nerves and causes them to retract.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not apply anything sharp to the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuity extends to the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	but let the medicine be prepared, as if it were washed in clear water and mixed with rose oil, and also washed in clear water, and other herbs according to this manner, and moist plasters.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cutting it open and binding it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	and if the wounds are deep and infected and full of pus, then pierce them or deeper still.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut, and blood flow stops, then disregard it, and apply heat, and cauterize the wound.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the colors, and the breath is preserved, so that the flesh goes, as much as the heart on the edge of the throat, and do not touch the throat but return it according to its natural form;
et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then the strict fasting, and leave it for no days, and then apply remedies of treatment until it is healed;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then the latter;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and if there are pieces of bone, if you can remove them all, then do so; but if you cannot obtain them, leave it until the wound suppures and heals on its own;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with the powder I mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones or a fistula in the wound, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne:	If it is a blow from a spear or a knife, and the wound is very deep, then pay attention to whether any air escapes from the wound; have the patient breathe normally.
saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	you then know that the wound is mortal;
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and if it is not very deep, and the blood flow is fresh, do not apply the powder immediately; do not bind it tightly for the bleeding will return to the body and cause the patient more harm.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor;	but I apply an attractive remedy, and bind it twice a day;
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors;	and if you have no remedy, place a piece of cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture, and let the patient lie on the wound for three or four days, or even longer.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne;	if no spasm, no shaking or pain in the body occurs;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the bones returning to their proper place, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Cure the wound with various remedies and others, as long as it is healthy;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule;	and if it cannot heal, dig deeper until you find a fistula;
si la cure si com on doit.	if the treatment is as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is shallow or deep, on the front or back, then treat it as follows;
s’elle est grans, de cousture;	if it is great, by stitching;
et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	and if it is small, by powder, and if it is tightly pressed into the bone, and has broken parts, then it may clean the wound, and strengthen it if they are defective.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they are not defective, then leave it to heal, and lighten the extraction.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds in other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	disruption of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures in the belly are great, medium, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from the great wound never let any intestinal tissues protrude, or the nerves of the intestines, which causes external infection;
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	and the stitching is more delicate, and no smaller wound is as bad as a large one, because one does not apply pressure to the intestines when stitching them up, unless they are sewed together tightly from both sides.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II.	because the intestines quickly swell and feel painful if pressure is applied when they are not yet healed, and because it is better to move slightly with smaller wounds, so one must first reset the intestine to its original position before applying pressure like with other wounds.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four manners:
les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	The two common stitches are used in the stomach stitch, and the stitch for other wounds of the body, and there are two other specific stitches that are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	Nevertheless, the stomach stitch is more precise, and I will describe each one and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres:	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine protrudes, and it is an easy matter to close, this is according to one of the four manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	for because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to injury.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it up in this way:
moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	soak a sponge or soft cloth in hot water alone, or boil water with vinegar, lemon, and spices, and wrap the intestine while it is still swollen.
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and never use constricting wines, but rather heat it gently until it is deflated.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	And when you see the swelling depart, if you have a moist or hot and bad wound, then it becomes easier for things to enter, a little at a time.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a slight cut with the instrument used to treat hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	and the first treatment is to move the bone, that we must not cut without great need;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument for the fracture:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if it cuts into the couch (or bed) and does not divert, then look at its shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound has enlarged and the intestine bursts out, if you can return it to its natural position in its proper place, do so, for that is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	When the wound is large and located on the lower abdomen, it is necessary to have the patient lie on their back and elevate their legs higher than their head.
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then put the head and heels higher than the affected parts, and also, when there is a rupture in the abdomen, place your attention so that the wounded part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus we must administer what I say to large and deep wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	For small wounds, make them as if you were equipped, then take in your hands a gentle medicine that heals all the rupture with its touch, and close the lips.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and this is the common method of stitching: you pierce a needle or several, according to the amount of space in the wound, then leave two spaces at the top of the wound, and insert a needle with strong thread into it.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	and pierce both joints of the skin with the two points of the scalpel, which is to go through the skin from inside, as long as you make it pierce from this part, and bring together the two points of the scalpel in three parts.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	then stretch a double thread around the needle from both parts, then bring together the two joints of the wound properly, and then leave two spaces, and insert another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not cease to do this according to your need for needles, until all the wound is constrained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	and let the needles be of medium thickness, between subtle and thick, for the subtle needles take hold of all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter properly.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	because they need to be medium;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not push the needles too far through the flesh and skin, that they do not puncture and open the wound before the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then remove the needles, so that they do not disturb the patient when sleeping, and put bands or cloth over the wounds to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is sutured.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	and this stitching method with needles is more suitable for small wounds, as it requires only one or two needles.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second stitching is common and consists of assembling the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of cloth together with a needle using a strong, medium thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	and when you have stitched these four pieces together, return the needle to the beginning point where you started, in the manner one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a minor thread.
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This suture opens the wound, and I sewed a wound that had been cut by a knife on the stomach, which was more than one palm wide, and it extended from the intestines another two palms, and the wound was in the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed completely within fifteen days, and he was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they marveled that he was alive, and it was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with any treatment, for I was in a place where none could be found, neither any remedies.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply a warm compress to the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it is healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture:	Now I shall tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle, and the thread from the healthier part, just up to this one inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	when it has pierced the center precisely, if you want to close or stitch or wherever you have pulled out the needle, and then pierce from the other side inside up to this one outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as a tailor sews the fur, and once you have satisfied one side, you take up the other until the stitch is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of stitching, which Galen rightly calls "the natural join," is like what others do who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the principal satisfactions to the other principal part in this manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	stitch a needle or a thread of wonder nearby, and make the single prong pierce only through one side, leaving both satisfactions' threads.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the weaker part until it reaches the inside, just as much as is necessary.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce both parts from the weaker side until it reaches the inside, in two other places where there is a miracle on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the most effective method of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	These words should be heeded, and no one testifies otherwise; the belly must be sewn with needle and thread.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must push a needle from one side, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corsets.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, it is the most difficult to sew compared to other openings in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout;	and it is that when you open a fresh wound and all its blood, so that the flesh has moved, it is necessary to close the intestines and stitch it.
puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	then apply the burning powder, and the fire will move it, but if you place any dressing on it while the wound is still open;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and take the thread, and make it secure, and close the wound;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as you would any other, until it is healed;
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and if you have no medicine, then apply, as soon as it begins to move again, a clean cloth, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you do not need other medicines for more complex conditions when the wounds are simple.
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and if you doubt that the wound does not extend to the principal members, it is necessary to apply a light bandage in hot oil or rose oil, and place it around the affected area, and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	and if it causes pain or cramping in the bowels, and this often happens, then give them enemas of red wine, especially if the inflammation reaches the intestines.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and he pierces it from within, and knows that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestinal organ, called "jeun" (fasting), cannot heal when it is inflamed, and this is due to the weakness of the veins, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the nearness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the wound gushes with blood, it should be pressed back as soon as possible, just like the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres;	and if it is old and has turned black, it is necessary to keep the dark part still, so that no more blood comes out, because there are veins and arteries there.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	then cut off what is between the bones, and hang both feet down from the opposite side of the wound until it opens up to facilitate the extraction when the blood lets go.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bowels
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in no man, for I have seen a nobleman wounded in his belly by a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it was a wound on the right side of the stomach, which festered and became a fistula, from which emerged excretion and flatulence.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied the treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to be subtle until he was healthy, and his limbs were healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would not have pain in his stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there is no harm, but it requires better dispositions, diets, and beverages;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and they should not attempt any experiments when there is a small wound in the intestine, but rather tie it in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	take a large piece of cloth, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the cloth has opened its mouth, place it between the two lips so that it pulls the mouth open.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	and then cut off the head of the cloth, and this should hold so that it cannot be released, then place another piece of cloth in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely sealed.
et cout la plaie.	and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere:	If the pain is sharp in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a way:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	take the end of this intestine thread, which is well spun, and then tie it to the end of this fine linen thread twisted, then wind the thread on the needle, and sew the intestine, and rearrange it in the rupture;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this method of stitching with stitches is no exception but according to the path of destiny and hope.
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it affects one of the vital organs, there is no treatment effective unless it be extremely subtle.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	or whether it is a fistula, wherever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	You know that every wound or abscess, when it opens, is generally called a "fistula," especially when it is covered with hair and deeply seated.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	And a fistula appears according to the truth of its nature, hard and white, where there is no pain, and it is also smooth like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and it never becomes clear or open, sometimes thick and other times thin.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	never too cold, and sometimes too hot;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes:	and I have spoken of the division of wounds; that every wound which is not clean, and there is no fever, it is only out of one of the nine causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, from the smallness of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its evil nature;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is a hard fever inside, and on the lips, which does not allow any healing;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	you have too much bowel wind;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	your bowels are overfull, and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	this medicine is not good for treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	because this corruption is a way of pestilence;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	because the sluggishness of the region causes delayed digestion, delays health, and is innately bloated;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	You have veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already described all these causes, signs, and medicinal treatments in the relevant sections.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula which is performed by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula occurs in all parts of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	for there are fistulas that affect large veins, arteries, and nerves, or the liver, intestines, bladder, any of the ribs, or the spine in the back, or any joint in the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it occurs at a part that belongs to the main member, and has similar joints.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas of this nature are difficult to heal, and there is nothing but hard work and ignorance.
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if there is no fistula that does not come to the place I mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure and understand it, then take a piece of iron or steel, if the fistula is directly in line with it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	and if the fistula is twisted, try to insert a thin piece of cloth or a small tool with flexibility, as the plug will bend and move around the curvature.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	and if it has open wounds and you cannot close them tightly with bandages, then wash it through one of the openings, for moisture flows from one opening to another and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	then squeeze it firmly in your power, knowing if there are bones or nerves, and feel it completely, and ask the patient with pain where they feel it and the location.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and when you truly know the location, and it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or any of the places I told you, then cut according to what I said, and remove the inflammation and the corrupt flesh that is inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	and then the cure as long as it is clean, and if the fistula is well dug out in the right place, it is necessary that you fill it completely, as much as possible, and then apply moist bandages with a medicinal ague, and keep them on the top of the fistula until the medicine corrodes the excess that is left at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply hot compresses with healthy garlic, as long as it is clean;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if it is not clean with that method, as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve does not affect your principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackening, remove it as soon as the corruption is gone, then treat the wounds with care until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	and if it is not healed, and the bone remains bowed as before, know that you are not allowed to proceed further.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	if it becomes exposed and you want to go deeper, removing all the corruption, then restore the joint.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If this is not the case, know that the corruption is too great, and you cannot repair it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other force than to leave it to nature;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there is a small corrupt bone that you can pull out with tweezers, and if it is extracted with a suitable tool, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, leaving none behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if moisture makes it contrary, there is no error or fear, if hot and humid and cold, and release the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	And if you cannot remove them for an hour, then place something purifying over the wound, and let it stay until the bones are rotten around them, and then they will become lighter on the bones.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie;	and if it is a large bone, like the leg or thigh, then remove as much of the corruption as possible until all the blackness is gone from the bone, and then close the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large amount of decay within, it extends to close to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it is necessary, cover it gently and protect it until the decay is healed;
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurs in a person's leg, so that you may take an example from it and receive aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	It was a young man around 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to something within the body, causing materials to gather at the leg, and he suffered from a large abscess that would not open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	but the excess because of their foolishness increased so much over the abscesses that they corrupted many matters, and became fistulas, and there were many ruptures throughout the body, causing bowing and moisture within.
et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and many more cases I witnessed over two years, and there was no wise man in the art of healing, until I was called to it, and saw his leg and the remedies by which he was cured, and what corrupted through the ruptures within the body.
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the skin of the young people became red, and had the color of a citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these gaps, and then I examined all the gaps, and I found that some came together against each other in every part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	I quickly prepared a tool, and chiselled into one of the gaps until I discovered a portion of the bone, which I found corrupted and pierced, and the corruption reached down to the bone itself.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I examined what I had discovered as the corrupted bone, and thought that there was no other corruption, except for the one I had found.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to heal the wound with potent medications for a long time, but it would not close.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I began to recognize and discover the bone as it was before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and healed it, and then I secured it, and focused on fusing the joint.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not until I had completely healed the bone, and gently pulled it to its original place, then treated it with medications.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it healed soundly and securely, and never wanted to repeat the operation again, except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and for the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For in the evacuation of blood, it often becomes completely healed, and a hard callus forms in its place, and is of good disposition and causes no harm or pain at all, neither going away nor coming back.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be handled in this way:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	take hold of the ligaments, and strain the end of the bone that opens, and command anyone to extend it upwards;
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and tie another, thicker thread to the first one, and attach it to the bone that is now detached, and pull the bone upwards, until you remove the broken piece, and expose the bone at its natural position.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place I a piece of wood between the bone to keep the corrupted flesh from opening.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to examine carefully as one can see and feel the corruption, and sometimes another way.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in one place or throughout, then expose the flesh entirely.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	then place wood between it and then gently open from one side to the other of the corruption, leaving the bandage tight around the corruption as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, remove the corrupted joint, and the bone it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, and there is no other way to remove it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or the ankle, and it is very strong, but nevertheless you must inquire into this corruption how it affects you.
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in every way that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve contradict you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and knows that the saw and the threads to cover these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for this reason, it is necessary to have the right tool for each task.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and knows that the work will show you the tool you will need, according to the knowledge of this art and the testimony of the ways of illness.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you think of the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	with fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The joint dislocates either due to pressure from within or due to external force;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	and when you have treated that corruption with medicinal remedies, and they are ineffective, it is necessary to immobilize that member until the corruption disappears, so that the patient may be saved from death or from the greater evil of permanent damage to the limb.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	and the signs of this are that the limb turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackening, the corruption spreads from member to member, affecting the entire body.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If you hastily cover it, and if it is due to the penetration of some venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion, a snake, or similar, and the wound is deep in the head, if you do not allow enough time for it to heal, do not let it come near your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes near the hand, if you dislocate the joint, so that the wound does not reach the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	and if it reaches the arm, if the dislocation is at the shoulder.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if it passes through the knife, it is death, and there is no cure stronger than the quantity of its virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	and thus do the same when rust or stone comes into contact with it.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	if it comes in the first joint, then cut after the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes from rust, cut off all of it.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends the leg, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other cause but to bring the patient to death.
