et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and the method of binding or wrapping the member: if you fasten it above and below, extend one minister from below upwards and another from above downwards, and you loosen the band that is between the two liens with a broad spatula, until the bone is exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	then bind or wrap it, and place each side with a cloth, so that the bandage does not touch the healthy tissue, and cause further injury and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And if the bleeding occurs when you open, cauterize the wound harshly, or place any restrictive powders upon it;
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then return to the treatment until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a strong ligature, and heal it as long as it remains healthy;
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	and I will tell you if it returns to the same place as before;
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	it will have a blackness that seems burnt from fire, and this decay begins first in its two big toes, spreading throughout the entire foot;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the bone feels the heat, it covers itself with a protective covering, and becomes healthy.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and after a long time, the corrosion or pain from the hand returns, and it comes to me, and I place things that repel upon the purification of the body, but the corrosion cannot cease.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and it seemed to me that I should cover the hand, but I did not want to hope for repelling the matter.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible;	and I also doubted that if he cut off his hand, he would not die, as the strength of the man was weak.
et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he becomes completely desperate, returns to his land, covers his hand, and is healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have no other objection than that which is done otherwise, if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess forms in the fat tissue, and it lingers so long that it causes great gathering of bowels.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it bursts and pierces, causing the bowels to rupture and remaining in the body as if they were a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and the skin that is above is as delicate as fine cloth, and it does not adhere to the bone or nerve, and such a condition is called "healthy," and is not called "fistula.
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it extends to the bone in a curved shape, it is called "fistula.
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is such that you must strip off all the skin around it, especially when it is delicate, just like a fine cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and do not hesitate because of its putrefaction.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you believe that the flesh hesitates, and the corruption is not entirely removed, and the flesh is dry and hard, then treat it with a warm bath.
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	examine if the breasts are swollen and the bowels emit a foul odor, then give them a cleansing with Egyptian medicine prepared as follows:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	take equal amounts of ash, oil, and litharge, and heat them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and then take according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and enemas the breast, and extracts the gap.
et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	leave the medicine on for two hours, then extract it while squeezing.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this several times, until the breast is cleansed and the pus is extracted.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never use enemas with water and ashes when this medicine is not present, and take ashes from the vine trunk, pour water over them, then strain it, and use it for enemas, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patient cannot bear it, neither Egyptian medicine nor water from ashes can help, if he is enemaed with water and honey, or has a little bit of litharge ground in it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	or you should enema him with honey and sweet wine, for honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine helps to aerate the health.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and when you have done this, and you are sure that the sins are well cleansed, then he should be enemaed with what causes a certain plant to grow in him, and you should press it carefully, and apply it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	you should cleanse it with certain medications and remedies, whose properties I have discussed in treating wounds.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	and if the opening of the wound is too small, and the canal of the clister cannot enter, you should widen it slightly with a hot iron and apply a poultice of Egyptian or basilicon medicine until it is widened.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the wound is too wide, so much so that it causes great suffering to the patient or prevents the clister from entering, and if the opening curves downward or upward, then the bandage should be applied higher or lower accordingly.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when the bowel is completely relaxed, it does not allow anything to enter.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the wound as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to its lowest position, for when the bowel is completely relaxed, it does not allow anything to enter, and if you cannot cover the wound as you see appropriate, arrange it thusly:
que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so that the bowel moves slightly downwards, and does not leave any part of the bowel behind.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain;	and take consolidating medicines to apply to the wound, and lay them on the linen cloth that covers all the wound.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	then take a smaller force near the hole in the chest where it is wider, and apply gentle dressing on another cloth according to the size of the hole, and place it over the wound hole in the chest to ease pressure, and do not remove the large outer cloth for several days.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and the one who is over the chest wound often removes it to ease pressure, and knows what comes from the wound, whether it's blood or pus or something else, or digestion, or undigestion.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when the medicine has been applied in this way and you see the nature that springs up at the wound, then know that the healing has begun, and bring it closer to health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	and then undress the wound in the morning or on the third day, and when you dress the wound, change to another bandage, and renew the dressing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast is bent downward due to indigestion after many days, knowing that the breast will not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons manifest after a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	For there are people who late at night put their wounds to bed, and others who do the opposite.
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if he has an indigestion or a sharp pain in his side after many days, knowing that it will not go away.
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	and if he cannot bring his side to heal, and it is distant, then apply medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue as a final treatment, for there is much vitriol within it, and this is the last medicine.
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take the final treatment, and apply it with rose oil, and mix it with old wine of equal substance;
puis le confit et en use;	then confirm it and use it;
et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	and this same mixture, when cooled and thickened, without the presence of garlic, you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind it, and sprinkle it over honey while it is still hot.
et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and then I wrap it in cloth and place it over the breast, and never administer without first mixing with long roots of licorice, which is also like flour from oats and chamomile.
et en use de simples ou de compostes:	and use of simples or compounds:
broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	Break them, and make a powder, and add the honey I mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	and if the cure is lengthy, and this cure does not heal it, then know that the corruption has taken hold, and it presses on the bone, or makes the joints hard, or damages the limbs.
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the cure for the fistula, as we have mentioned above.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	A gangrene is an abscess that forms under a nail of the hand or foot, or occasionally in other areas.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and when it is neglected and left unattended, an abscess forms, and it oozes and flows below until the root of the nail runs out, or perhaps it oozes everywhere.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it brings corrosion up to the bone, causing intense foul-smelling pain, and the wound becomes broad and has a purple color.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	If, as we have mentioned in the previous discussion, you treat it but the treatment is ineffective, then you must remove any excess debris from under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	Cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy, and the nail is uninjured.
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and if the nail quickly turns black and begins to prickle, then you must immediately place a stick under the nail that is pricking, lifting it up, and gently squeezing it out, applying burning and corrosive medications on top to remove everything.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat the wounds as long as they are clean.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it off and remove it, for as long as the bone is corrupt, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if you see both bones corrupted, cut them as described above, and treat them as long as they are clean.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is twisted and contorted, and it causes great pain, then you must treat it first.
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	then cut the nail with a sharp tool diagonally from above, and be sure that the cut does not reach the skin underneath the nail, as the patient would feel too much pain.
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, put something cold on it to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain should be so severe as to paralyze the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	He who is born without hands, or has them extremely fleshy, and perhaps has part of his bones missing, and never any fingers, and none are born in the root of the joint—in such cases, birth must take place elsewhere.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	He who is born with no pain should not be silent, and he who is born with pain in the joints may remain silent.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the incision on the fleshy part should be light, in this way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer:	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure:
si te tien dou coper.	if it keeps you covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born with or develops a deformity, it is necessary that you first hold the joint firmly up to the bone, then dislocate the bone to a suitable position, and finally treat it as long as it remains healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The deformities that come at will affect the entire body, either from birth, or from wound healing, or from a burn by fire, or similar conditions.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	If it is necessary to cover the closed one, then it must be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then place between two moistened cloths or sheets soaked in rose oil, so that they do not adhere;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You should insert between two delicate pieces of cloth, as long as the wound is sealed properly.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If dislocation occurs at any of its joints with the palm, handle that wound as appropriate.
des vils	Des vils" translates to "from the
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Their veins are thickly enveloped, filled with melancholy excesses that affect several parts of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more often occurs in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things, than with others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary for you to administer purging of the bowels, and then clean the wound in the temple.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres:	The treatment for this is according to two manners:
l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	one is with cautery, and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and another way is that you open the vein and draw it out completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The procedure is as follows:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	first, raise the affected leg with hot water, until the pain is subtle, then stretch the sick leg from above the knee to the ankle.
puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	Then open the vein in the arm, or in the leg, or in the thigh, with a wide cut, then carefully and slowly extract the black blood with your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it, and command the patient to eat foods that produce dark, black urine.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and washing when the veins are filled, causing harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The treatment of it is according to this manner:
reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	Lift the leg of the ailing patient, if there is any hair, then submerge it in water, and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you have no bath, heat it over the fire, and then apply it to the vein from the top of the thigh or at the ankle, wherever it is most painful.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then open the skin at the point of the pain, and scratch the vein from each side until it appears raw when touched.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems as if a white string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois;	then turn the right of the bone, as long as it is raised from the skin, and then bend it gently to the oncine, then cut in another place on the opposite side, above and below.
puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then scrape the skin over the vein until it opens, then gently raise the edge, as you did before, and bend it to another oncine, as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille;	then take another size, or as many as you need, then the light one, and cut it with the right sharp tool, then treat and lift until the second size is reached.
puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then extract it bit by bit, until it comes out completely, then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and if you cannot pull and lift it, insert a needle through the entire thread twice as thick, tie it and pull, press from one side to another until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and ensure it does not tear, for if it tears, it cannot be pulled or raised, causing harm to the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset;	and once you have extracted it, place warm, moist wool and rose oil on the wound bed.
et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and dress it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie;	And if the vision is contracted, twisted, and rolled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it with care but do not tear it.
et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	and take it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The way to do it is to make the eye so sharp, and not cut, unless it opens the vein.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and it is very sharp, because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but since it is thick, as we have said, and this is its form:
de la voinne civile	of the main vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in hot regions where no herbs or trees grow, and on land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	and perhaps it occurs in another part, namely the legs, and this happens due to rotting that comes from beneath the skin, as it creeps within the body winding and turning, entwining between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein appear, it is that there is a very great swelling in the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude strongly, as if it were a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	When the joint opens, it is necessary that you wrap around with a piece of cloth from one and a half to two fingers thick, and then tie it tight, leaving the cloth on the leg, and every time there is no opening at the wound, if it constricts around the cloth, and the new bandage.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut a part of it and wrap the remaining part, without covering its root until it is completely healed.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	Because if you touch it, it returns to its original state, causing abscesses and corruption in that place, leading to great illness.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For which reason, it is necessary to treat it gently and little by little until the pain disappears entirely from the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse;	and it is never this vein when it is treated with long, or very strong, hands; and a great honor came to me, from whom it reached ten palms in length, and if you touch it, it sinks or opens up, and penetrates to the bottom, so that everything comes out.
et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	and empty the matter within, and administer to the place drugs that cause putrefaction for no more than a day, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains;	And never touch this vein with raw hands, especially when it opens at the joint of the foot or the toe, and much cracking and popping occurs;
cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	treat it as we have said above.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that are born between leather and bone.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is called the "bull disease" in our land because it often affects bulls, and it is a small worm that appears between the hide and flesh, spreading throughout the body upwards and downwards, and it feels very hot from one limb to another, until it breaks through the hide where it was. It then causes a powerful discharge.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is caused by putrefaction of certain humours, as they gather and wind around the intestines, worms, slugs, and ascars in the stomach.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil;	and doubt arises about the nature of his illness, for as it spreads through the body, it ascends to the head, and reaches the brain, perhaps returning and damaging the brain.
et ceu avient maintes fois.	and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it healing and draining, it cannot be done unless it has passed.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	If it is necessary, then you must lie the limb above and below with a strong binding tightly, then cut and pull it out, and turn it inside out in the wound, and do not remove it, if you cauterize it with fire until it heals.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm it does is when it bleeds, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming close to the wound, quickly pull the hair forming a curl from below, then cut and pull it out.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and it is necessary for the patient to purify the body with solvent medicines for harmful humours, and to abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre;	This disease is called "vakerire" in our land, and it is a pain that comes in no particular member, but can move from one member to another.
et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and I have seen what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I noticed a small swelling in the vein of the breast.
et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	and then I noticed, the sight rose up in the shoulder just as a worm, more so than anything else, as bright as silver when it cuts into another.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	the pain departed from that place and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then after a short while, it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other breast.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then it told me that it twisted around the body again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled much at how she moved from limb to limb, for I had never seen this disease in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	Nevertheless, I wanted to know why the pain moved from one place to another, but I could not understand it, as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and I thought it was because the woman had dry skin, and the veins exposed, and because of this constraint of breath.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and did not seem consistent to those who are delighted, with moist skin and veins concealed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	And when you see this illness heal and the patient feels the pain, if it opens as we have said, then press from above and below firmly, and continue until this constrained breath at the joint leaves.
et cauterize le leu;	and cauterize the place;
et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	and if you do not see it on your own, then treat it with those who expel winds as if they were bad pills, or pills of serapeum, or similar ones.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary, according to their appearance and the part of the body they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	Their diversity is such that there are those with great points, and small ones, and curved, and solid;
et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and some with two edges, and others with tongues, and those with pieces.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres:	and those that break in any limb break in two ways:
ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or it breaks in the principal limb, such as the head, body, liver, lung, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it breaks in any part of these members, then you will notice the sign of death, which I will tell you below.
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	you must be careful with the extraction of this arrow, for death comes in many forms afterward.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if this bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not completely extracted, pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	And the sign of a weak mind when the arrow breaks and pierces the bone, and the swelling appears on the head, is when there is loss of vision, darkness, watering, redness, inflammation, redness of the tongue, spasms, confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles;	and perhaps without feeling in the nostrils or ears;
et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance loses the word and voice;
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and from the moist wound there springs a white fluid resembling pus, and also as blood from a wound;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign appears, if you hold to the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not stuck together.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it breaks or withdraws is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it were stuck in hard, non-empty substance.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance, the patient's sitting may become mute like the pulse, and there is sudden black blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	so he knows with certainty that death is descending.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never improves is that foam without pain flows from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's skin turns pale, and they breathe heavily and stop moving.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes;	And if the arrow comes out in the cover of night, it leaves small marks.
et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire;	and it causes great pain and great sorrow, and sighing.
et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	and it moves all the members of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, perhaps something from the undigested meat may fall out.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow pierces the abdomen, and there is no sign of recovery through the intestines, then there is little hope for treatment or in removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor:	And if the arrow pierces the bladder, the urination jumps and comes out, and the patient feels intense pain.
saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	you know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs—as they feel and are affected by pain and swelling in the throat, shoulder, and back; as well as in the joints and legs—are safe according to various arrangements.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, for this reason, you should do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man that an arrow fell or pierced through the root of his nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and I pulled from the other side through the fat of the ear, and it became well without pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles;	And take a sharp arrow, that has fallen into the grease of oil on paper, and the arrow is removed, so that only the tip reaches the wood, and it was an arrow large as a bowstring, all blue without ears.
li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	it became healthy, and no ill accidents came upon it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And take an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow with ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I loosened the beard, and I pulled gently as I took it, and the Christian became healthy.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And pull out an arrow from the body, which had pierced its belly, and thought that he was dying.
et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then, after thirty days, if his condition does not improve;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut the arrow, made an incision, and pulled it out, without any bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see a person with an arrow pierced through their back or chest, and the wound is deep;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	and hold the arrow inside it, and do not change its natural positions, nor find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And look at another man, who has an arrow in his face, and the wound is deep.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor;	and thus he suffers greatly without pain.
et mout d’autres semblans.	and many others like him.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie;	And remove an arrow from the body of a prince, who had it stuck in his neck, and was slightly inclined to the right side.
et estoit li saiette toute reponue.	and this arrow was entirely withdrawn.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	I was called to treat it after it had been fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very deep.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I approached it with great subtlety, and felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and it felt sharp and painful behind his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I thought it was from the point of the arrow I applied a soothing poultice to the place, because the swelling did not go down.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the arrow's shaft.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis;	I applied the heat to the wound for a long time, soothing the patient, so that he felt the arrow inside his flesh all day.
et il le me dist.	and it came out.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	I applied a strong corrosive medicine to the wound for a long time until it opened, and I tested it, feeling the point of the arrow that was stuck in the flesh.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjust the opening of the wound with that medicinal oil until the head of the arrow becomes visibly visible.
et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and it took more than three months for the wound to heal, and then it became so inflamed that I had to use pincers, pulling from both sides, but it wouldn't come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	then I did not cease to try and invent new tools until I found a set of well-made pincers, according to the shape that will be described at the end of this chapter, while I worked on it, and kept opening and closing the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the most skilled judges believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I then restored it, and the wound healed, and the patient was entirely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	Or, I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you place your care on what I do not say, for the books cannot encompass everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	but the most skilled surgeons consider even the smallest thing and what is present and lacking—correctly assessing new works and nine instruments—when dealing with strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I say that arrows do not leave the members where they are embedded, but according to two manners:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the place where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and the one that comes out from the other side where it enters, is an arrow entering into the flesh, and will never come out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not come out now, leave it until the flesh around it decays and becomes easy to remove;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, it cannot come out, if it is left like that for no days, and moves each day.
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps, and if it does not jump, it pierces around everywhere in a subtle way, until the swelling around the joint is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the top, it goes all the way to one of the bellies of the brain, and none of the accidents that I have mentioned affect the patient.
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If you cannot pull it out, but leave it as long as it remains even after several days, for if the arrow goes all the way in, it's a deadly wound.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is embedded only in the bone and does not come out satisfactorily and remains in the patient without any further harm, as long as the skill of pulling it out allows.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit;	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be pulled out, then apply warm compresses around it, as I have told you.
puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	then heal the limb as long as it is healthy.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is withdrawn into the limb deeply and one cannot see it, then apply all efforts to extract it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, use any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if you cannot open the wound due to its tightness or the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone, nerve, or vein left, then close it as long as the wound remains large.
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and try to extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that hold it, remove the charred part from both sides as much as you can, and then break or bend the barbs of the arrow until you can draw it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and skillfully, without breaking the arrow, draw it out more forcefully.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot at once, pull it until the joint around it becomes loose, then treat it, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the symptoms of bloodletting work against you, then administer as we have said about treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement;	and guard yourself from incision near nerves and veins, and in any way you can extract the arrow without danger, whether quickly or slowly, firmly or gently.
et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	and place the patient according to the condition he was in when the arrow entered, for it is the greatest aid, and if you cannot, then follow what the signs show.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another direction, where it opens anything within, or the skin is swollen in that place if one sees or feels it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai:	then cut around it, as much as the pincers can grasp, and then extract it:
si saut fuer maintenant.	if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, turn your hand roundly, until it enters the bone, widening the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	and if it cannot be extracted, leave it for now and then try to extract it again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if the arrowhead is stuck in the flesh, it presses against the entire flesh.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument;	and if the arrowhead is removed, you must apply pressure gently, as if you administer a sharp instrument, so that the tip of the arrow enters the wound of the instrument.
et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and then press firmly, and if the arrow is embedded, insert the instrument with a pointed end to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you clear all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, and then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow comes out in the stomach or bladder or side, and it is close, you may cover over it, if it doesn't hurt.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and guard yourself from sealing the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then sew the wound, it is a skill.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the pliers used to extract arrows resembles an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres:	And there are many ways:
grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	great, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape [of the arrowhead] pointing downward is like the feather of a bird, to drive to the tip of the arrow, as this is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of claws for driving and gripping, if this is the case:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir:	There are 31 veins from which one gains health, of which there are 16 main ones, that is to say:
II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	II beat the muscles that are after the ears, which are called the "soft" ones.
et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans;	and the second arteries that are in the temples, appearing clearly;
et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the veins that are in the joints of the limbs, called "aspirations";
et li voine que est emmi le front;	and the vein that is on the forehead;
et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the vein that is on the back of the head;
et les II guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two glands that are in the collar.
et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the upper lip of the mouth, and these veins are called "augerich.
et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and the two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras:	The veins that one commonly sees are 'V' in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic vein, which is located on the left side of the body, and common people call it "vein of the head.
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»;	and the joint is called "fast", and it is composed of the head and base, and the common people call it "vein of the body".
et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and the base is located on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is below the ribcage, and it is the one that heals, opening clearly on the pulsation.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains;	And the saving vein is the one between the little finger and the ring finger, and if it rains (i.e., swells).
et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes:	and in the leg and where the foot are three veins:
l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit;	one is so placed beneath the ribcage on the left side, and the second is at the ankle on the right side;
et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the vein called "nesse" is in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg, there are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The healing of veins located behind the ears is beneficial for old catarrh and migraine.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre;	and the qualities of the healing, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the patient's head and rub the affected area with a rough cloth;
puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief:	then tie the patient's collar tightly, until both veins behind the ears become visible and hang down from the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	take them in your hand, and where you feel the pulse below your thumb, press gently;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	then take the lancet, and cut through the vein just below the bone, then gently your hand along all the vein upstream, and open and close it well two or three times, and let out the blood until you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then strain and hold it, as long as it is healthy;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	The health of the two arteries in the temples is like an old and severe migraine, and the eye accustomed to tears at the corner.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of a good healer is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient tightens his collar, as long as both veins are open wide;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feels the coldness beneath both hands, and then presses with a signet.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then gently apply pressure to the vein at the top of your right index finger, insert the lancet beneath, and draw out the blood, first from the vein above, then the vein below, just as you did with the other two veins, and allow the blood to flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then free the patient, and place your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee;	and then form a ligature, and leave it until it is healed.
et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and we have spoken there of their treatment and extraction, as the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein on the forehead is just as important as the healing of the head in cases of old facial diseases, migraines, and redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is such that the patient tightens his collar, twisting it until the vein opens.
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this form:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another object, allowing blood to escape according to the amount you see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then gently release the patient's collar, and tie the vein tightly until it is healed and free from any broad opening of a flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus;	Nevertheless, one must not let the flames be too fierce.
et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	and do not let the healthy one go astray, for the bone is hard, and perhaps it will break the flames when they are subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healthy of the two veins that are in the arms should be aided with these, and at the wound, and at the itch, and at the redness, and at the swelling in the eye, and the diseases of the face.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their health is such that the patient squeezes his neck without twisting any ligament, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then the healthy one, and make the wound heal, slightly longer than the flame, but not too wide, for there is no need.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise;	and if the flame is subtle, it may break.
puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	then make the blood flow, as much as needed, and then bind it with cloth, securing it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	The wound of the vein near the nose is very valuable for colds and sudden illnesses, and facial diseases such as migraines and redness that appear on the face, especially when they are old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	and the quality of the health is such that the patient squeezes their throat, then pulls their nose to your left hand, and takes the fine, long flame and inserts it between the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein will not open well enough, and the blood will begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not remove it too quickly, and let the blood flow as needed, then bind it for a night, for it is often restored quickly.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The holy water of the two eyes helps in the narrowing of the eyelid, and at the onset of illness, and with many diseases, and inflammation, and corrosion, and herpes, and pimples.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the quality of the water is such that the patient draws their collar close to each other, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	and if the master is on top of the patient's head, and the patient sits on a chair, then wash the vein with long water, then treat the blood with temper, or as much as necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle;	then repeat the process on the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and gradually tighten the veins to prevent strangulation of the patient.
et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	from the healing of the veins
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the veins in the lips above helps to open the mouth, and aids in the cure of gum corruption, lip cracks, and pain and swelling around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of healing is such that the patient should sit before you, and tighten his collar as I have said.
puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right side of the mouth and the other on the left, and you can recognize them by their black color and the small, black lines around them.
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Handle them both then, and if you do not know and are in doubt, take the larger one from each part, and make also two incisions, one above and one below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	From the cleansing of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The treatment of the veins below the tongue is of great help after treating the neck, and it is for the tightness of the throat, and for eye diseases, and for mouth ailments.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of healing is such that the patient should bite between your hands facing the sun, and relax the tongue, and look below each side for a dark vein.
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then make both healthy, but do not cut too deeply, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres:	The veins through which blood flows, commonly healed, are healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	you cut through all the inflamed tissue with a wide or thin knife, as you would make incisions, and it is called "aneisil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are wide and thin according to the thickness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	It takes on the form of a bright flame if it is very renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it is necessary to open the clear, broad veins that contain much blood and are filled with pus.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the form of olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicately pointed, and is for healing the delicate veins where there is subtle citron-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The vein from the basilic, which is one of these veins, is very helpful for diseases that are beneath the throat, and the collarbone, and the chest, and the abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and the healer must carefully clean the vein and wash it with the artery below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it affects an artery, and blood flow is disrupted, as I have said, it needs to be stopped.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and the flame should not be aggressive, but cut it as gently as possible.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the vein does not open clearly, it is necessary that you extract it and choose another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras:	or you should not touch any part of it, but heal the vein in place, between the arm and the shoulder.
elle apert manifestement;	she opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and apply the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you recognize the place of the wound, it is necessary that you extract the arm, touching the place until you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the place with a sign, then bind the arm, and apply the flame gently.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere:	and beware that you do not injure the artery when you see the bone enter, for it is the artery.
eschui la donques.	then avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it bulging at the top as well as the urine of a child, and its skin is red and delicate, know that it is an artery.
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	then hurry, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the skin remains intact, as it often does.
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides;	He lies with his arm outstretched, allowing it to remain thus, and does not move the patient.
et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient;	And if the wound is not healed, it will decay, and there are no remedies at hand, especially if the artery opens up, as with a retraiment's chief.
et estainche li sans.	and heal the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fig bark, cut it, and take one half of it and bind it firmly to the other side.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien;	if it is not attached, that is good.
se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	if it is not, then treat it as we have said, with powders that prevent blood clotting.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	the clotting is not overly grasped in various arrangements due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	The surgeon of the vein should cut it away if it helps to drain blood from the top and inside of it, because it is composed of both basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and the surgeon should wash for the nerve that lies beneath, and if he does not cut it through completely, and it cuts into the nerve, then it swells and inflicts great pain, and in some cases cannot heal.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil;	and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any place due to its subtlety, then you must use a more precise instrument.
et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and avoid using your strength.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two bones, make it open wide.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The treatment for headache involves drawing blood from the head, which helps and eases the pain.
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary for the healer to prick with olive oil or myrrh fire, because this is the safest of all veins, as it does not disturb any nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek the lightest vein, and do not be concerned if it hurts the first time, and repeat the process.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and sometimes the eyes swell up in certain people, without any reason, but it causes no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound healing is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	The first thing you must know about healing is that it is not only a means to restore health but also a way to prevent future illnesses.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute:	and healing should be done through one of the three veins:
c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	that is to say, the cephalic vein, the femoral vein, and the basilic vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and one must heal in the beginning of prayers at dawn, and in the afternoon and in winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	and one must heal the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healer who is entrusted with illnesses has no fixed time, but whenever it is necessary, day or night, in all seasons and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it is not advisable to heal children until they are twelve years old, nor women who have given birth for less than four months up to seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	One should not consider the old people who have passed sixty years as healed.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	And when anyone wishes to become healthy, in any way, it is necessary that he cleanses the bowels with a light enema if there is much feces retained, so that the veins do not draw out excess waste harmful to the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	One cannot become healthy who is overly accustomed to eating meats, nor those who are greedy, as long as it persists.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and purifies the patient after colic, vomiting, abdominal distension, frequent defecation, much sexual activity, hard labor, watching, fasting, and this due to a weakness of either the weapon or the body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then gently draw out the humours, if they are thick, through food and drinks and medicines, if you have such a means.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	then enter the bath, if nothing prevents you, to draw out the blood gently, and cleanse the vein from within, as we have said.
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and guard yourself from work, and pain, and lust, and similar things that day.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	and be calm and joyful, and make sure the wound is healthier than that of anyone else. Rub the arm twice or three times, then gently pull the bandage from above, for if it is too tight or loose, it will not heal properly.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the limb with both hands until the veins swell and you feel them.
