puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	then moisten the wound with a drop of old oil, then place your left-hand finger on the vein below the limb where you want to heal, ensuring the vein does not burst or get injured.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	For there are veins that flow like strings when healing, and if they are filled with pus, when you apply the fire, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and so one remains in this state.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if it opens a vein, if the wound is too tight, then it is necessary that the healers be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin;	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good;
se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	if not, it is necessary to repeat this again from the beginning, close to where it was first done; if the limbs are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient is afraid, let it be for one or two days, and do not bind the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus;	perhaps he gets abscesses instead.
ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	he should not bathe again until he feels better; then he can continue the treatment if desired.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if it is a small opening, he should make it smaller gently and you will doubt that there is not much blood as you see, for the same fire coming out of this very opening goes straight to all parts.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez;	and make it slightly inflamed, so that the veins become swollen.
car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	Because this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the vein inflating, do not immediately recommence the wound treatment, and apply a little oil, for it lightens the body of the blood, and the oil is moved in this vein along with the blood.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer the oil in each wound that you heal the veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu;	and it also acts as an antidote and draws out evil when applied to the vein.
si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	if subtly the bone moves and spreads when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	And if there appears a large abscess, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small and you are not skilled in its opening, then quickly place a moistened sponge with hot silk over it and hold for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary that you do this after the discharge of blood from the vein, and if it remains at the site for several days without any black or green color, then it does no harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see, place on it something cool or cold, such as aloe or myrrh mixed with calamine, shows, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique:	And many times an abscess and pus appears at the wound of the basilic (nerve).
met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	then place your hand on it, and if you feel the soft place at the compression of the hand, then this is where the appearance (of the abscess) is most severe.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere;	So be careful that you do not place anything that we have said, for sometimes it cuts off the artery without notice.
mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	but he makes an embalmment with dry materials to harden the joint, then applies other remedies until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each pain according to its quantity and the color of the pain.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges;	For if the skin is pale, let it be left until it turns red.
et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez;	and if it appears thick, leave it until it becomes thin.
et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is fat and strong, and needs the extraction of blood, to make a larger wound, with wider incisions.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and to those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is better to heal them slowly and frequently, and one should heal them by cutting across, not puncturing;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this healing method is free from corruption of blood and nerve damage, and it is more effective to heal from a long way rather than a wide approach.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates;	and for those whose body requires healing, it is necessary to give them a mild pain from the juice of pomegranates;
s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	if it is heated, then treat with bloodletting 3 or 4 times, and if it is of cold complexion, before the healing, give them mild pain from syrup made of grapes, or honey syrup infused with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the sight of blood after drawing much blood, it is necessary that he inhale a broth of horse, and a subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things as we have mentioned in the previous section or chapter on fainting for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to straighten his arm and heal it better later, if it is weakened by much bleeding, he should treat it gently and gradually, according to the amount of its continuous power.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wishes to straighten his arm after the first dressing and has a strong bruise, he should heal it for seven hours after the first dressing or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to be healed from another side should be healed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre;	For there is much blood inside the body which has been heated, and it brings fever.
si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	if it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the wound as much as possible so that it completely heals.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	then you must fulfill all the conditions for healing, and place your hand on his pulse when he is well, so that death does not come in its place, which often happens when the healer is negligent.
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not appropriate when you see the arm dislocated and make blood come out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press hard on top.
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	if he is weak, he should stretch the arm slowly, for it would be harmful.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois;	but he should let it be for as long as it heals the second time;
ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	or you should apply it to the tip of the flame until the blood clot that blocks the vein is dissolved and removed, then cover it with a small piece of cloth soaked in water, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to drain the blood a second time, do so either in the same place or in another vein or arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is healthier in place of the vein in the head because it is composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing is that the patient should immerse their hand in hot water until the veins are red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	then bind it gently so that the vein appears well, then immediately through the healthy flesh, neither too narrow nor too wide.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the wound wide, and ensure the healthy flesh is close to the joint of the hand, and if blood cannot flow out, then immerse the hand in hot water and let the blood flow out in the water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if this does not work, do not immediately push the hand back into hot water, as more heat will only cause further damage.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the health of this vein is safer than all other veins, having neither artery nor nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The health of the saving vein in the right hand is worth against all liver diseases, and this is how it is done:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	stretch the hand and immerse it in hot water, as long as the vein is swollen, if you see it;
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and hold the hand across, and if you grasp it from all sides, there is no pain;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and do not hurt the patient too much, for the nerves are completely bare of flesh, and then apply the hand with hot water, so that the blood vessels become frozen in the wound, and cannot escape.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as best you can, then apply oil and string to seal the wound firmly, and thus do for each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sick person should hold the remedy in their left hand to treat the mouse disease, and do it just as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The remedy for the spleen is effective against all diseases that affect the body, such as diseases of the uterus, retention of fluids, illnesses of the kidneys, and old diseases of the joints and legs, and similar ailments.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet;	And the quality of their health is such that the patient should immerse themselves in hot water and rub the vein until it bursts, and apply pressure over the joint.
et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot they apply much pressure.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	Heal then, where you feel pain, whether it is larger or smaller, at the shoulder, or at the ankle, whatever moves you.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant;	And if you heal it on the foot, be careful with the nerves that are beneath, and also heal it across, as if you were binding it.
et soit li flaimes anesil.	and so the flames will subside.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound will not heal, immerse the foot in water and allow the vein to drain completely.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the healing takes place for the first time, then repeat it a second time above, because the wound is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do the same for the wisdom of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The vein's lion is at the foot's joint, and its purification causes pain in the back when it is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne;	And the quality of his health is such that if the patient enters the bath, he should stretch three times above the ankle, otherwise the vein will not open.
et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	and if it opens, stretch the vein in all ways that you can, and pull through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is worth that you grasp it, for the vein is safe, and it is much relieved by many hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you do not hold it firm, any healthy thread of the muscle that opens or closes the foot and leg towards the little toe, and be careful with your nails.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint;	and apply pressure firmly against the blood to see how much there is, then loosen the tie, and place cotton on it and tighten it.
ele est maintenant sanee.	it is now clean.
des sainies de ventouse	From the suction of the cupping glass.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre;	Vacuum cups are made of horns, or iron, or glass.
et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres:	and ventilation is done according to two manners:
ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	or by puncturing and drawing out blood, or without puncturing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres:	And this ventilation without puncturing is according to two manners:
ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	or it is with all fire, or without fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief;	and the ventilation done by puncturing and drawing out blood is done in twelve to fourteen parts of the body, so that one part remains entirely still at the head.
et li autres est emmi le col;	and the others are in the neck.
et II autres en II costeis dou col;	and others on both sides of the neck.
et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and the cup (or suction device) from under the chin.
et li ventouse des II espaules;	and the cup (or suction device) from both shoulders.
et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the cup (or suction device) on the knees.
et les ventouses emmi les II bras;	and apply leeches to both arms;
et les ventouses des II jambes;	and leeches on both legs;
et les ventouses des II chevilles;	and leeches on both ankles;
et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and the leeching does not treat blood, but rather small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken anyone, as is done with vein-sucking.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it is not advisable to apply it, neither hot nor cold, in any disease that arises from excess, as long as the whole body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if, due to necessity or habits, it needs to be vented (i.e., let out), we should do so every hour at the beginning and end of the month, and in between each time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are some who, when they need to let out (gas or air), have such a heavy head.
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and if it is for those who have a fullness and redness in their face, head, neck, and darkness around the eyes.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and those who have a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and taste blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and if there are any who think, see blood, pain, death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially in the middle of the month, we order letting the air in after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The physician of the museum helps in the great pain of the head ... which come from dislocations, and it does not suit that this be after the evacuation of all the body.
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and this application is in the place of the physician of the head, and it does not suit those of a cold disposition, or who have scrofula, for they do much harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason, it does not suit the old or those with cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who is cured often becomes obtuse, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cup a little lower in doubt of obstruction.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	The ventilation of the chest is beneficial for health and life, and because of this, it helps to tighten the muscles, and opens the channel of the womb, and relaxes, and promotes filling.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it is necessary to know when to stop, because if it grips too tightly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and body pain.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique;	The ventilation of the chest, if it causes pains in the head, eyes, and temples, and constriction, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and disrupts the health of the sinew of the basilica.
et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it is necessary that you instruct the healthy person to press his hand gently, not to cut the artery, and prevent blood loss.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche;	The evacuation of the jaw is useful for mouth diseases, and for gum corruption, and similar ailments that are in the mouth.
et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	and it is in the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The symptoms in the shoulders indicate a disease that arises from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	The evacuation of the veins is as useful as three veins in the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the healthy one not to cut too deep, for the flesh is bare of bone, and knows veins and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire;	The cupping glass that is on the nape is worth much for bleeding from the fundament and diseases of the veins, and it should be large, made of iron, and must be used skillfully.
et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit;	and if, by chance, it was too thin, it would break.
et i fai grans plaies.	and it causes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors;	The suction cups on the legs should be applied tightly, for they draw blood from throughout the body, and they relieve the long-standing pains of the joints, and of rheumatism, and of the bladder, and restore circulation.
et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	and they affect the second ribs, and the ankles, yet they weaken the body after long use, and cause pain in various ways.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc;	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: you apply it first while it is empty, and then suck firmly, and place it steadily, and move it equally, without stopping, until you see the red and inflamed color of the blood, and open the flow of blood.
puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez:	Then apply pressure, and remove the suction cups, and take care in the arrangement of the skin, for there are some with such hard flesh and clear pores.
si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes;	if it is necessary to strike only once, then it is necessary to make wide wounds and deep ones.
et suce legierement.	and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois:	And if the pain is intense, it is necessary to strike twice:
la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	The first time to discover the way to draw out the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois;	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike three times.
et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	and when we want to draw out blood little by little, it is enough to strike only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent;	And if we want much blood, we should begin often.
et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and if the blood is thick, striking deeply will make it flow, and quickly finishing, the veins will be perceived, especially with those who have tough, hard skin, and are hairy; one must apply oil to the suction cups both for opening and closing.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is a matter of burning, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from cucumber seeds;
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it is in the veins, with watercress oil, or lotus oil, or chamomile oil, or any other similar thing.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amber oil, or balsam, or donkey oil, and similar substances.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is tender and has large pores, it does not require oil to be applied, but rather should be washed after a rinse with rosewater, or cold water, or water from a morelle (a type of berry), or water from a cucumber, or porcelain water, or any other similar liquid.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those with excessive moisture should rise from it using myrrh water, and sumac, and similar substances.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with excessive fluid buildup should drink old wine, or vinegar water, or anet (a type of plant) and chamomile decoction, or other similar things;
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II;	and they should not attempt to use the cup (for bloodletting) immediately before or during a bath, but rather after the bath, one hour or two.
et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and do not sleep after the drainage, and it is necessary that he washes himself, both when he needs to drain and when he has been drained.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	and take care that he who is sick has a temper that is neither too cold nor too hot;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	it is necessary that he applies cold things, such as apples, grapes, endive and lettuce in the heat, and similar things;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and eats plums, and juices of chestnuts, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should drink syrup of honey, and moderate perfumed wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat herbs and small birds and pigeons.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he drinks more than he eats.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it is necessary not to give any hot drinks or spices to anyone at any time before or after opening the windpipe, in order to comfort the main limbs.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and it should be done carefully, but those who are cold should not drink hot drinks.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne;	The suction cups that are used to harm are those placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and podagra, and on the stomach, and the bowels, and the legs, and the hips, for this member does not tolerate being wounded directly, and it is only done forcefully to draw blood from one member to another, as we do with the nipples when nursing.
por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	to reduce the viscosity in the member, as we apply suction cups to the stomach and bowels to ease the pain.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and relieves the pain when there is compression or stone, perhaps by attracting the compression with its virtue, or by displacing the stone from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement;	and thus it is done when one places it on the liver and intestines when there is wind retention, and these suction cups are emptied to only suck;
et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	and never should they be heated together with fire, and never should they be filled with cold water, as in cases where there are abundant tears, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot water, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the cup (ventouse) administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And it should be two and a half palm lengths wide, with a small hole around the middle as thick as to fit an needle, and it should be made of iron or softened so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and tell him to place a rod of wood or iron across the wound, so that a cloth can be wrapped around it, according to the size and age of those who suffer from them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suckers of children are different from those of the old, and thinner than the fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	and one must thus place this sucker over the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	take a cloth of wax or linen, and place it through the sucker across the rod that is inside the sucker, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the sucker, preventing it from burning the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the affected member, and your fingers should be over the opening we mentioned, so that when you want to, it goes in and remove the suction cup.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and take up the line as before, and repeat often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup, which is used for treating pleurisy, and all acute conditions, there is no opening or gap, and it should not be applied unless it is filled with water, and then placed on the affected member.
et c’est li forme:	and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	According to their smallness, they are only treated with cups in places where it is not possible to apply suction, such as the lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in naked places, such as the groin or nipples, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the cupper is such that when you find veins that are clear, smooth, and without inflammation, they should be taken.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place a nut in hot water, until they are well-soaked and have no wind or stomach issues;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then make the vein and phlegma (or varicose veins) healthy, and rub the limb until it turns red, and apply bandages.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and if they stop paining and swelling, it is a sign that the vein or place suitable for cupping can be applied, then apply it, as it is very beneficial afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If that does not work, then gently lift the dislocated limb from the side, and then with water, very well, and then apply pressure.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and hold the eyes steady too long after the operation is complete, if a moist linen cloth in cold water is placed over them, and left there until the wounds are healed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the wounds multiply, apply crushed vinegar, or gall, and similar substances, until they are healed.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can place half-peelied beans on the joint and leave them until they adhere to the bone; this will now heal.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more skill, take other wounds.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And if the roots will not take hold, rub fresh blood into the place, or insert an needle until the root enters, and then place them back, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will sprout.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are sprouting, sprinkle a little aloe and silk dust, or ash, and they will grow now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book on fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is about the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear reader, that the foolish eyes shed tears from this chapter, which they have never seen in any of the ancient books, nor read any letters about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and for this reason the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found any good of it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing of it, except for the knowledge from ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have acquired the knowledge, and through experience, and through the habits of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is appropriate that we begin this book with a prologue that outlines the essence of the words and chapters where the wise men apply their understanding and focus on truth; so that those who are tested know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twist or sprain comes to any part of the body, it is necessary that you quickly tend to the patient on both sides, if nothing else helps, such as weakness of the body, or fever, or old age.
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois;	or if it is very close or too cold;
et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre;	and warm things, such as hot baths, and cloth from silk and chamois, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that clog the veins with blood, until you are certain of the heat of an abscess or the swelling of a member;
si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	if the patient returns to suffering from a previous treatment, as it had been used before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be given foods that do not cause excessive flatulence, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and peas, and veal, and offal, and ox, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because part of the wound's healing causes movement, and more often the fracture.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that broken bones from the old and frail cannot be well healed or joined together according to their nature due to the immobility of the members, nor those that are too soft, such as the bones of young children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant;	but there is no cure, reset the broken bone with strong claws that separate and join the member together, as long as it becomes strong again like it was before.
et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	and do not touch any part of his body, and for this reason, it is necessary to feed him with nutritious food as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture is of two kinds, one from the upper part, and another from the lower part, and in this chapter I will tell you all manner of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There is also a fracture that goes to the bone, and another when sharpening, such as the cutting of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, then it is a fracture with a very small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each person has their own way and their own specific tool for recovery, according to the memory that comes to them in their place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and the fracture of the bone is known because the joint is twisted, and it opens well when pulled outward, and responds to the pressure of the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and when there is no twist or pressure, and the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can have curvature, or fissures, or small breaks.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not need to move it with your hand, but apply medications that will follow, and then gently hold it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that occurs in an artery, and where the two parts are separated, it is necessary for you to now set them equal, so that abscesses do not form from them.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if abscesses form from them, if he leaves them for no time, until the abscesses are calmed.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces;	then set it equal to the movement that you can gently and surely make, and know that the restoration of what is whole is easier than the restoration of what has been broken.
puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	then hold steady, as it is needed afterward.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken bones, if they are pierced from two sides, whether it is the hand or foot, or at your hand if it is a small member, or at the joints, or at a joint and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the member according to its natural position, so that when the parts of the broken member are out of alignment, reset them with all your might, and ensure through your skill that no further damage or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and adjust both joints of the bone according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien:	And if it feels good to the touch, but it seems not properly aligned:
si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	if you dress it well, without straining too much, not pressing as those who cause a hot and contracted abscess in the member through their own will, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is at its limit, gently comfort the patient so they do not move it, neither waking nor sleeping, nor turning, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and ensure that the limb is securely held so as to feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, except momentarily, and it is important to ensure that he does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set correctly, so that no crookedness comes when it is healed;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the damaged limb can be different in size and shape, and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans:	For it has small limbs, like arms and legs and similar ones.
si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	it is necessary to wrap soft and delicate linen cloths around it.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe:	and those that are thick, like the soles and legs:
si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	it is necessary to wrap with a wide and firm bandage, for the wide bandage embraces the whole limb and tightens it equally from all sides so that there is no gap.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then he applies slight pressure, three times or four times according to the limb, and gently holds your hand throughout the joint, then moves upwards over the fracture and exerts less pressure, allowing the fracture to slightly separate.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and softens the joint little by little, pressing deeply into the healthy part of the limb, then takes up another joint and returns to the one above the broken bone.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then goes back to the part below the fracture and holds it gently, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first line above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place it between the thick strings of linen or cloth, as long as it is entirely even, then tie everything above with a bandage, and then put your carefully made stitches on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	If there is an abscess or swelling, apply a hot soothing agent to it, which reduces the swelling, and leave it like that for several days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then stretch over your stitches, and use a strip of thin material cut from a sharp knife, or from the wood used to make splints, or palm leaves, and conform it to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the thread which one places on the break be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and be as long as necessary for the member, whether small or large;
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then tighten it over the threads as you did in the first chapter on the break, and then tie it with an additional thread, as in the first chapter on the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins;	the tighter it is bound, the less it moves;
et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	and it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the thread is too thick, as I have seen in works of people who make their threads with twisted linen cords, it is a great error, for the thread cannot be equal if it is too thin, and it is not suitable for there to be less than two threads per inch of space.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is angry because of the pain from the stars after dislocating their joints, he should place them in a hot compress of lint or other soft cloth so that they do not get infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by fracture, and the bones are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all the broken stars on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	Because when the limb is large, it is not suitable to insert threads for more than five or seven days, or as long as the abscess above is healing, according to your judgment.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion:	and now let us consider the ancient methods of splints to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists:
et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and take flour that clings to the walls of a mill, and mix it with enough egg, and make this paste, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of splints for restoring fractures in various positions, especially among women and small children, as it is neither too hard nor too soft.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion:	Another method of splint for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists:
pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.;	Take some barley meal, and honey, and lupine, and poison-oak, and gum Arabic, and mix them with water;
mirre et aloes, ana V З.;	mix it with mirror and aloe, as V suggests.
alechil VIIII З.;	add aloes VIIII as directed.
et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef;	and make it into a powder, and mix it with egg albumen;
se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	if the patient's complexion is hot, use this paint, for it is of good composition, and heals broken bones painfully, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion:	Another method of splinting that is effective for twisting:
pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.;	take a cloth and make it moist with vinegar, and apply it to the wound.
mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.;	use mirrore (a type of medicinal substance) and aloe, as described in chapter nine.
acaice VI З.;	use willow (a type of plant) as instructed in chapter six.
bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	prepare aromatic Armenian powder (a medicinal compound) as instructed in chapter ten, grind it well, and mix with vinegar or an abundance of egg white, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure:	Another way to plaster joints and dislocate bones from their sockets, soothing the pain that arises, they use chisels on the bone, and breaks.
pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Take another new cloth, and soak it in hot water and oil, then place it on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cyst splints do not restore proper function, but they are good for alleviating hot abscesses and safely extracting bones that cause pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez:	Another method of plastering that restores broken bones:
pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Take dry figs leaves and land pavot (opium poppy) leaves, crush them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plastering for the restoration of broken bones, and to alleviate the return of the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie;	Take the root of vismalve, chamomile, violet flowers, fennel flour, of each part in equal measure.
et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	and grind, and mix with wine, and warm the limbs, mix it with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plastering for the restoration of a stubborn, hard-to-heal abscess on the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie;	Take the roots of vismalve, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and fennel, and violet and chamomile flowers, of each part in equal measure.
et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book that to restore a broken member, one should use a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, stating it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen suggests that to restore a broken member, one should apply warm, dry substances such as myrrh, aloe, incense, and similar things, as we have mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor:	Another method of splinting that is effective for both injury and pain:
pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Take feathers and horsehair from shorn men, or goose down, and silk thread, and cut them equally, and grind them, and make a plaster of it and bind it tightly.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu;	And then, after some time, loosen it slightly and take care that the patient feels no pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place.
si ne lou deslie par mains jors.	if it is not loosened by skilled hands.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant;	And if pain comes to the place, or itching, with no rest or swelling, then hurry and dislodge it, and remove the plaster immediately.
et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	and take a light cloth, and a sponge with moist sea water, and dip it in water, and raise the limb up until the itching stops and the pain is soothed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it up with a bandage until you are certain that the abscess is hot.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant;	and rest the inflamed member, and relieve the bone pain, then resume gently, with a little plaster, and do not strain it as before.
et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	as gently as it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is red, swollen, painful, and filled with pus, and you need to apply a poultice and bind it, then repeat as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII;	And if nothing of what we have said applies to the member, then do not release it until after three, or four, or five, or seven days.
et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	and never leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals and approaches the adjustment of the bone to the joint.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant;	then you must hold it more tightly than first, and thicken the flesh as I have said before;
et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	and if you see the joint is set firmer than necessary, know that no improvement can come from it.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	soak the dislocated joint in hot water every time you reset it, and do this three times a day, gradually opening it up.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement:	by this effort, then gently encourage the limb, and patiently wait for what the skilled healers do, who restore the damaged member.
c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	This is evil, and if it causes great fear, I see no other way than to leave it and do it right.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various methods of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many types of fractures, various shapes, and the causes are diverse.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust;	For there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and the bone splinters completely through to the inside, as if cut with a knife or club.
et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatchet-like".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»;	Or he strikes the bone with the spear without piercing it, and this manner of fracture is called "absolute";
et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	and this wound is great or small from these two fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a throbbing, or swelling, or cuts from stone chippings, or blows against stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a recent fracture, which approaches the skin just beneath or on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound that is healed in the bone is as subtle as a hair, and the fissure is small, it is then called this fracture "capillary";
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres;	and if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or an arrow, or any similar object, and the bone fragment enters inward, and the joints are bent as if a blacksmith were forging on a forge;
si entre li piere dedens.	if it enters within the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this is more common in those who have moist heads, as with infants.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles;	and occurs in all these ways of fracture that small pieces become detached as if they were.
et je em parlerai en son leu.	and I will speak of it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all the ways of dislocations caused by traction on them, and the inquiry at close range, and by the corrupt flesh above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is noted because when the bone is discovered and rubbed gently, it opens the dislocation, revealing the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be wary of accidents with the patient, and if you notice any ill omens, such as vomiting, loss of senses, stiffness, paleness, ague fever, or other symptoms appearing in various combinations, then it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any alarming accidents and hope for a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the swelling comes to you first, and it is in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this happens, if you hurry to remove the bone on the seventh day, so that the flesh under the bone is corrupted, then the complications arise that we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi:	And if the fracture of the bone reaches up to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in this way:
et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and you should press the patient's head with great pain, and expose the bone in all ways that you can, and smooth the wound more gently than you can, and if blood comes out when exposing the bone, or an abscess begins, assist with what is necessary, and fill the space with moist, oil-soaked cloth.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc;	and keep the wound at rest until the abscess is calmed and be sure of the absence of blood flow.
puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige:	then begin to separate the bone, and this is done according to two ways of working:
l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	One method is to press against the narrow opening from the front, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I use another treatment even greater than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde;	And the second method is that you have numerous openings of varying narrowness, some pointed and others wide, and they are made of indurable iron.
et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	and gently open it, so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os;	And if the bone is hard and dense, you must drill around it gently, so as to create openings with care, without penetrating too deeply so that the tip does not go beyond the bone. It should have a margin or curve on top to prevent the tip from going through the bone.
et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test;	and it is necessary to have many, so that each comes back to its place in the expectation of the bone, so you have time for all tests.
et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	and this is the form of the three types of delay:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez;	The quality to perceive around the broken bone is that you apply delay to the bone, and return to your tasks until you know that the bone is perceived.
puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures;	then apply the delay elsewhere a little later, and do so all around, then make cuts with incisions in the space between the parts of the bone, and do it more subtlety and lightly, as we have said, while you are holding the bone in your hand, or with any of the tools you have such as pliers, pincers.
et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	and remember that you must not touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced the bone with the trepan, it is necessary that you feel the stiffness that is delayed from the bone to all other tools resembling an incisor, but it should be more tense and more subtle than any other incisor.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens;	and if it delays nothing of the small bones, nor any scales, gently remove them with the instrument.
puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	then dress the wound with bandages and care as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus;	And another method of treatment is as follows, which Galen says is safer.
et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	and speak very loudly, as he says.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you expose a part of the bone, either where the fracture is open, and when you have exposed this part, place the tip of this curved scalpel beneath it, whose shape is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os;	And do not cut from one side, but the acute part is on the second side, so that the cuts are towards the bone.
puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	then strike gently with a small hammer, so that you lightly knock the bone around, and be very careful of the tissue below.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is detached from the bone, gently pull it, for it can be pulled off without pain or harm.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not reach the skin, and the bone is cut only from above, leaving small fragments, it is necessary to remove these rough edges with a fine rasper in sufficient quantity to make each part as suitable as possible, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you encounter great raspers (tools) and then more subtle ones, never stop doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement;	For each of the other hair cuts or subtle breaks, you must treat according to its location.
et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	and this is something that is never fully answered for him who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if satisfaction is desired, you must press a linen cloth according to the quantity of the wound, soak it in rose oil, and place it on the wound.
puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil;	then take another cloth doubled over two or three times, soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth.
et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	and make it lighter than you can, without burdening the patient, then apply another bandage over it, and do not tighten it too much so as to only touch the wound.
et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses;	and leave it thus for a day or two until the abscess is calmed down, then untie it and administer medicines such as roots of lily, wheat flour, incense powder, aristol, and similar things.
et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	and from these things make a powder, apply it to the wound, and administer foreign medicines without harm;
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice;	and ensure that the wound is always clean, do not leave any uncleanliness, nor allow it to form bumps, for when a bump forms on the skin, if it breaks open, it brings great harm to the patient.
car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	for when you apply sharp, harmful things to it, they do not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is questionable without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if discoloration appears due to the medicine applied to it, that its virtue may take effect, it is necessary that you mix a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and wrap it in a cloth, and apply it to the affected area.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then the treatment of manners of healing that are necessary, as long as he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os;	Knowing that the two parts of the upper arm are never broken, except one after the other, because they are two bones.
et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	and this bone is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it bends or twists severely, then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should bind your little finger or make a slit in the flesh of the arm, and place the same fracture into your index finger, and by pushing with force, until the bone returns to its natural position.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	and do this gently, and ensure that the patient feels no pain through your actions.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the upper part of the bone near the joint, and the bones cannot return to their original position, it is necessary that you place a slightly thicker rule across the top, so that the bones align correctly.
