Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	If the fracture is from the second part, and it happens again, then quickly restore the first state on the same day, if you can.
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	if this is not possible, then after the seventh or tenth day, when the swelling of the abscess is reduced, apply to the wound clean linen bandages, if the fracture is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est;	or you apply another from another side, if the fracture persists;
et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	and make the bandages so thick that they fill the gaps between the stitches.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say that no restoration is required if the bandages are soaked in butter, and changed each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin;	I do not think this is right, but it is necessary that they be moist when preparing bandages of egg whites and mill powder.
puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	then remove the bandage until the bone is hard and the cartilage stiffens.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi;	And never use goose feathers or other materials in place of bandages, and if the wound is filled with pus, it holds the rupture, and the breeze blows the patient's pain away.
or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	or make sure you see well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses appear at the wound while you are treating it, apply a poultice or moist cotton in olive oil or in a small container of eagle's blood.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if abscesses do not come out, apply a poultice from the outside with flour of cumin and incense powder, preserved with honey and egg yolk, then place light bandages on top, without tying them.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	and if the broken bone is small and broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then clean the fracture and treat it with hot things like poultices and applications of heat, as appropriate.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if he does not have a wound deep within the nose, then treat it with care, and insert wooden splints until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	from the dislocation of the mandible
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is dislocated and there is no external wound, and the fracture is only slightly displaced, and it is not broken into two pieces, but only out of place, then if you gently know how to handle it, it can be reset.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide;	If the fracture is in the right side, you should insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient with the malady.
et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	and if the fracture is in the left mandible, insert your index finger of your right hand, gently push the fracture back into place, and use your left hand to pull it out, equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is severe in two parts, you must administer an extension to both parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double;	And if the movement of the teeth causes a rupture, then tie them with a thread of gold or silver or silk, and apply a plaster to the broken jaw, and cover it with a double cloth;
et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	and place a large, well-made cloth or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the jaw upon it, secure it with whatever means you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet;	And if you see that the shape changes, untie it after three days and then reset it as it was before.
et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote;	and apply a plaster on it, with a powder from fine grinding or flour of chamomile, after you have removed the cautery.
et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez;	and apply a lighter new plaster, and if the plaster becomes hard, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until it is healed.
maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	often it heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, it is necessary to do as we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee;	And if there is both fracture and wound together, it is not necessary to remove any piece of the bone that has been broken.
si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	if subtly from the opening as suitable instruments to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And once you have removed all these pieces and it does not delay, immediately close the wound if it is wide, and place suitable bands on it to prevent infection, until it heals.
de la forcele	from the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres:	The force breaks many times, towards the shoulder, and the fracture is according to three manners:
ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer;	or it is broken and dislocated in two parts, and there are fragments, and it is the easiest to restore;
ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	or there is fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie;	And the work is as follows when the fracture is without a wound, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the aid that is broken with force.
et li autres estende lou col vers la partie;	and the others stretch the collar towards the affected area;
puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	then make the fracture even on both sides, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no apparent deformity or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit;	And if you need to extend it further, place a round, thick cloth or woolen spear under the shoulder of the patient, as needed.
et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	and gently stretch the limb, extending the spear with your hand, so that you evenly align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the bandage away from the wound because it is stuck, then it is necessary that the patient lies on his side, and places a medium pillow under his shoulder, and asks his attendants to lift the bandage towards the back, until the bone in the bandage is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus;	And then address the fracture with your hands, and if you feel the bone fragment, it is necessary that you cut through it.
et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as;	and gently try to realign the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined together in any way, then remove one of the incisions you have.
mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	but apply the full strength of this instrument to achieve satisfaction:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre;	and it should resemble a spoon, and not be too thin, and also as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work.
et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and he should say to the patient, as you see, one shoulder should be wide and the other narrow, just as the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bone;
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and when you are sure of the hot abscess, if you cut the wound, and if its opening is small, then you doubt the hot abscess, if you use cloth and bandages for the wound, according to their quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess forms, take a cloth dipped in rose oil, or aloe, or wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The straining of the bone, when it is sensitive to touch and has no dressing, is that you place on the bone a thin paste of finely ground powder and egg yolk, and then put light stops over it, and insert a spear under the joint if needed.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre;	then take a very wide bandage, one palm length wide, then place two layers on top of each other over the joint, and wrap it.
puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that the end of the bandage extends beyond the joint.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide;	and place the stick on the fracture, and turn the bandage around the collarbone, and remove the healthy armpit, and the painful armpit.
et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and reset each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture well, and you clearly see that the stick does not move on the broken bone, tighten it each day, and when the ties loosen, then release it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut;	and make the patient lie down on his side, and place a small pillow under his armpit when he is asleep, to lift the dislocated joint up.
si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors;	if you align the shoulder and lighten the fracture with the positioning of the arm at the collarbone, and do not unlock it until after a malicious accident does not occur for 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez;	then resume the plastering if you see that it needs to be done again, tighten it and leave it thus until it is healed.
et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	and it is restored in no more than 28 days, and to no one less.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	It is often the case that a broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal well and remains unstable, unless it is properly aligned by touch.
si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	if it is aligned according to the shape of the break and restored to its natural position in every way you can.
puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double;	then lay the shoulder gently on a soft, thin cloth, and cover it with a double cloth.
puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment;	Then place a wide and delicate blade, slightly larger than the shoulder, and dislocate the blade at no specific point on the shoulder, using the sharp edge of linen cloth so that the blade cuts evenly.
et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor;	and then tighten it with a great tight band firmly, so that the blade does not move from its place, and inspect it each day.
et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit;	and whenever it loosens, tighten it again and realign the blade if it is out of place, and lay the patient on their side.
et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en XXV.	and the shoulder is healed in 10 or 25 days.
Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	And when these numbers are completed, if you loosen it and be sure, for this is not an oss that will easily set itself.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone sticks out and is not removed from the inside, it pierces and causes inflammation in the abscess, so do as we have said to soothe the heat of the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the fracture do worse
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc;	The skin is never completely broken in the middle, but this happens rarely.
mais il brise sovent au defuer.	but it often breaks from the heat.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines to the inside, and the patient feels great pain, and there is no improvement, and sometimes blood oozes out, and it opens up the openings in the broken bone, and everything feels good.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back, and places a cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and aligns the ribs to the two hands, and subtly adjusts it equally in all ways so that the bone figure is as it should be.
puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve;	Then place on it plasters and compresses over the delicate salt or other light bandage, wrap it in a drape, and secure it to the broken bone so that it does not move.
et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint;	and straighten the ligament back to its original position, tighten it gradually, and check the freedom of movement every hour, relaxing it if it becomes tight.
et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures;	and if it needs to be released due to rust or itching that appears on the skin, or pain or abscess, act quickly, release it, remove the plaster, and treat what has come about in a curative manner.
puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	then reset the splint and hold it tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	from the breakage of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses;	You know that the breaking of ribs only occurs in the upper back and at the top, and they do not bend unless they are broken.
et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	and feel the patient well at the examination.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is such that you put the break back in place as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and hold it with a board, if you have such a need.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile;	And if the breaking of ribs is internal, the patient feels very great pain and a stabbing sensation, as well as weeping, because the bone punctures the tissue.
et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	and he holds the fingers, and touches and vomits much blood, which is of great illness, and the ancients have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if it is of those who say that it is appropriate to administer foods that cause bloating in the stomach to push out the fracture inward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not pretend that abscesses will not form if they have not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it comes back, healthy.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison;	And they say that none of us should use cupping glasses on the shoulder to draw blood, as it is useless; it seems reasonable.
toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	Nevertheless, there is doubt that the cupping glass does not draw away the excess blood from the shoulder according to the arrangement of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say none of you should cover the wound with moist wool and oil, and put tents between the ribs to equalize the space around it, then be cured of pleurisy, flesh, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac;	And if the patients feel great pain that they cannot bear through the bone where the cloth is applied, there is doubt in the patient, and it is necessary to cut into the broken rib cage and place instruments to preserve the satisfaction.
et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then one must cut the bone, pull gently, and stitch the two edges of the wound together, if it is large, and treat it with bandages, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu;	and if abscesses occur, place moist, oil-soaked rags on them and cover with a cloth.
et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and treat while the cloth over the abscess is still fresh, and place warm compresses on the affected side or where it is needed, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	Of the dislocation of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie;	No fracture ever occurs to the delicate collarbone without reason; it happens when it rains.
et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	and also to the sharp pain in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to a person, and you want to know if they will recover, be wary if you see their hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and unable to move or stretch them, and if you pierce them with an needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Knowing that it is deadly in many ways, if they are silent and feel well when you squeeze them and they do not hurt, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and the patient will be cured if proper treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit;	And if similar things occur to the sharp pain in the back, you must know if it is sane (curable) or not, if you notice whether the feet are weakened, and if there are accidents in the hands, and on the back, sudden vomiting and expulsion without will.
et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	and when it is remembered on the stomach, sudden vomiting without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is recalled to its back and wants to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz:	Knowing that it is mortal:
si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	if one does not work diligently on its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to pass, then it is a lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez;	And the treatment is that if there is a hot abscess, you apply rose oil or egg yolk oil to it until it is soothed.
puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer;	then place a comforting and drying poultice on it, secure it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest.
et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, as long as he is alive.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur;	and if any bone becomes detached, it is necessary to cover it with gauze;
et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then take the bone, and afterwards close the two edges of the wound with stitches if it is large, then apply a dressing with hot compresses as long as it is alive.
et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier;	and if the bone fragments are broken, which is called "shattered limbs," press your thumb of your left hand into them and place it level with the other hand, then apply plaster and bandages as needed.
puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	then hold it firm, and if there is a bone out of place, pull it back into position, and set the fracture, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	From the fracture of the bone of the spine.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief;	First, note that the bone in the neck (hainche) is broken, and if so, it should not have much diminution at the top.
et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	it extends down, curves towards the back, and brings pain to the patient in place of the break, causing swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure;	And the healing is such that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the break.
et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li;	and such are the fracture and form of it;
et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	and if the fracture is only at the head, then make all such fractures even, as long as they are in their natural form.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach until the restoration of that fracture appears.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve;	And when you have made it even, then place an splint over it, and then put a stick or rod of wood across it, and hold the fracture still so that it does not move.
et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	and secure the limb against the ribs on the inside, as long as the ligaments are even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit;	And if an abscess appears and is not touched, it should be left until the abscess below is calmed, and apply what we have previously mentioned.
et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident;	and then return to restoration, and tighten as appropriate, if there is no adverse event.
et c’est li maniere.	and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	dislocation of the shoulder joint
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres:	The aid (or support) is between the shoulder blade and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two methods:
dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	Don't do it unless you take a thick piece of wood, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege;	and bind the two pieces together, twist them upwards, and place the patient on a seat;
puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval;	then pour the patient's broken arm over the wood, until it is straight, and have them hold a wooden splint in place, then twist it downwards to any heavy object or have the attendants pull it down further.
puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	then place the splint against the break, equal to the patient's hand together, until the fracture returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another method is that we place the patient on his back and tie his hands to his neck, then instruct those assisting to apply pressure over the break in each hand, and extend them all equally.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too violent, hold the broken part firmly in place, and on the break, stretch each of the assistants to their side.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure;	And if the fracture is close to the top of the shoulder, you should place a moderate ligature under the bone, and another around the neck, below the fracture.
et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute;	and also if the fracture is on the side of the neck, you should apply a light ligature without effort, as long as the fracture is even on both sides, on the bone and on the neck.
puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	then even out the fracture, as appropriate, and tighten it, if abscesses form or pain persists.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess appears, do not press it for seven days, and apply a moist cloth dipped in rose oil until the abscess at the base is calmed.
puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein;	then press it, and the method of pressing is that you apply a splint to the dislocation, then raise the arm above the affected joint, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast.
et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	and apply the bandage, press on the affected joint and the arm so that the arm is raised, perpendicular to the body, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone has not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part;	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use a splint, and place a wider and stronger stick across the break, and leave two spaces between each stick, and let each stick be so large that it extends beyond the break on each side.
puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	then tighten the sticks, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the break, stronger and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit;	And if you observe the position of the sticks and their tightening, as we said, when you return the broken limb, and you doubt whether the abscess is hot, leave it bound for up to seven days, as we said.
puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	then examine each of the three days the wound, that itching does not swell or come to the surface, or the healing cannot come to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it is appropriate, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac;	And if no such accident occurs, then the dislocation should only be corrected after three or more days, and the patient should sleep on their back, with their hands on their stomach.
et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens;	and place the dislocated joint in a soft cushion made of equal parts wool, and every hour during the day or night observe whether the limb's shape is restored and its joints are not too tight.
si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz;	if the treatment is by the virtue of medicine, and he gives the patient the food that we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first subtle.
et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	and when he begins to recover, it is often severe.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout;	and it is customary that the aid and leg must be reset after forty days from the beginning.
et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	and then he must be dislocated and treated with baths and specific remedies to correct the position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is severe and painful, it may take up to ten days or two months to release it.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet;	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fossa," one smaller and the other following the direction of the hand.
et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi;	and the other is larger, and it is the one that is located below, towards the smaller bone.
par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	should the larger fossa break only, or both, and they become disjoined.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations;	When the smaller fossae break, their healing is light and swift.
et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	and when the bones are broken, if healing is poor, it is more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then a little gentle stretching and positioning them equally is sufficient.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort;	And if it is a large, deep wound, then it needs to be tightened more strongly.
et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor;	and extend it on the cushion, placing the palm higher than the other hand, and the small fingers lower, crossing the patient over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any pain.
puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	Then extend the attending physicians their hands to the distant part of his arm, or to the joint, and other ministers to the others above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then set it even with the eyes, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if, in the fracture, each piece is set in its place, and if there is none that holds the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place by doing as we have said before, then it must be cut off and the bone healed.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler;	And if with the wound rupture, I have spoken of it in the specific chapter;
si pren la cure.	then takes the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz;	And if, at the beginning of restoration, abscesses occur, I wrap them with a bandage made of rose oil and white wax, not too hard or too soft.
et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	and I wrap it gently, as long as the abscess is calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres;	Then remove the bandage and apply the plaster of fine-milled powder with plenty of egg, then place the nails, making sure the nail from the break is stronger and a bit wider than the others.
et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions:	and know that it must have 6 nails or arms in different positions:
soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II;	so that the break is in one of the bones, or in two;
et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre;	and it holds faster over the fracture than elsewhere, and for a longer time as it moves away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter.
et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres;	and the bandages that are over the fracture should be soft and moist, not hard or rough.
et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	and the thread, from which it is held, should be linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after no days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez;	And if no harm comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then it is necessary that you apply hot water to the limb until the itching is soothed.
et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	and let the member not be squeezed too tightly at rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then repeat the stretching, and if the ligaments loosen and the bones deviate, or similar things, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it slightly, and leave it for a few days until the swelling goes down, and then stretch it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said help the patient, then he should be loose for up to 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	if uneasy, then bind his hands to his chest, and make sure his collarbones are even, and guard against movement and reaching, and have him sleep on his back.
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 45 days, and perhaps in 10 days, according to the combinations and complexities of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You know that on the back of the hand and at the joints there are often small fractures, and it brings only pain many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient cuts a cross and holds it straight before him equally.
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	then places his hand on the extended board, extends the broken bones of the limb, and aligns them properly, until they are well joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	and applies poultices and heat, if an abscess forms, then he places a piece of salt according to the size of the wound.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	and is wrapped in a cloth drape.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the fracture is near the abdomen around the root of the plant, make a ball of cloth and command the patient to press it against his swollen limb.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	and then apply a long strip of cloth, and make the bandage as soft as possible, as large as the palm of the hand, and tighten it, as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the open air, it is necessary that you place a stick above and another below on the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it tightly all around the hand, and seal the gap between them.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	If any fracture occurs among us in the hand, it is the joints that are affected, so we must set them even as they should be.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and tighten with the palm, and if you notice a small, straight bandage that raises the fracture without moving it, use that.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the fracture is in another finger, just as it was described or indicated by one of the others, set them even and bind it with the healthy finger afterward.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	You should hold them all in place until they grow out, or put a splint over them as you would a broken bone.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and take care in the restoration and placement of hot abscesses, and protect those who come near them, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	from the broken hipbone
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The foot bones are often broken, and one can clearly see them when the foot returns to its normal position both in front and behind.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	and the restoration is when one binds them together over the break, and another from below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment;	And the patient lies on their face, then extends each limb equally to their side.
et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	and this is when the fracture is through the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the hipbone, one of the ligaments should be bound towards the knee, and others should be bound below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval;	And also if it is near the knee, then the ligaments around the knee should be relaxed and the leg bent downward.
puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	then place the splint with both hands, equally according to its natural shape, and then apply the bandage, binding it tightly around the injury so that it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure;	And if there is a hot abscess, leave it to calm down before returning to your work and treatment.
li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	The bandage is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus;	You should wrap around the fracture a bandage hard and doubled in two or three layers, remove the excess, then turn the leg until the heels reach the root of the toe, and pass a long thread between the calf and the leg, beneath the knee joint, and bring the end up over the top.
puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe;	Then turn the bandage to the leg and thigh, then place the splint on top, and put a stick across the bone of the leg.
puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure;	Then use the eighth part of a soft cloth between the leg and thigh to even out the pressure, then begin to tie three or four loops around the splint.
et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint;	and as you go higher on the splint, it should become less tight.
puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet;	then take the two threads that you have threaded between the leg and thigh, and tie three loops underneath, then return to the other side at the top with the thread, as you work towards the foot.
et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	and hold them still, if they do not move from their place, then leave it so, and there is no abscess or swelling or any other sign.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois;	And if it happens that it becomes dislocated again, and you notice it, then correct it as we have said many times before.
et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet;	and if there are fragments of bone that stick, it is appropriate to remove them, if possible.
et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer;	and if it is not possible to remove them, then it is appropriate to break the joint and pull strongly.
et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	and the treatment is as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras;	And never should the foot be broken in this way with stars, as is done in the case of aid or the arm;
toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	However, this carefully performed restoration does not please the patients.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the foot is restored in 7 days, or fewer or more, according to the diversity of dispositions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	You know that in the alley of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, even if it is only a crack or an opening, it affects every wound, and feels painful, and everyone feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet;	And the restoration is when everything is put back in its place as it was before, as long as it can be moved together.
puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant;	Then apply the plaster, and place a round stick, if needed, and tighten it appropriately, then repeat all the arrangements we have mentioned in other fractures, as for a hot abscess or anything similar.
si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	if one is involved in such an accident as it suits them, as long as they remain healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	from the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»;	Knowing that the leg has two bones, of which one is called "right" and not "mustelz", and the others are called "foscile";
et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	and it continues to break all the way to the arm, and because of this comes the restoration as with the equal arm, and all the work is complete. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg moves from every side.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bones are broken, they bend forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien;	and if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain, and one can see it clearly.
et torne desoz.	and it turns inside out.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement;	then apply extension, and set it equal, and tie the stars equally.
mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere;	but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are several pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter.
et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	and light according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz;	And when you have completed your task, take two strips of cloth as thick as a finger, that cover the leg on both sides, and are long enough to reach from the knee to the sole.
puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien;	then wrap it in two strips of cloth around the leg both above and below, and tie it tightly in the middle, so that the leg cannot bend to the right or left, and thus it is good.
et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie;	and no one should administer any medicine to the long bones of the leg, especially if it is broken, and he places the leg to prevent movement, and properly does this at the fracture where there is pain.
et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident;	and each day he moves the leg to see if there is an abscess or any other complication;
si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	if he treats it while it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	from the fracture of bones in the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones in the foot can be fractured and the toes can be dislocated, and there is no cure except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	And if a foot bone is broken and you see the bones pushing against each other, the patient lies with his bad leg on the ground as if he wanted to walk, then place your foot on top of his, holding where the bones are lifted, and press until they return to their places.
puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	Then apply the plaster and stop it up, and place beneath the belly, at the pit of both groins, a small table with two flat sides, then tighten it at the most recent healing, after you have wrapped them in drapes and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three days or four have passed, if he loosens the bandage, for you will find the bones even, either broken or discolored.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main;	And if either of the bones is not broken, but restored, as we have said regarding the bones of the hand;
puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment;	then place on the broken bone a steel according to the length of the bone, and be a little wider, then beneath the foot place the table I mentioned, and tighten it firmly.
et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet;	and if there are two or three (or more), break them, and place on each finger a stone according to their quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and tighten the table from under the foot.
et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	and if it is on the top of the table, towards the stomach of the foot, make sure it holds it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit;	And it is important that you do not forget the other things I have mentioned about other breaks, when we have said this.
et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	and protect each case as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	On the fracture of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier;	When the bones of a woman's natural structure are broken, if she lets the swelling increase, then she inclines her body to one side, and it is held from behind.
puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto;	then fill the swelling with cotton, and also put in large amounts of it as needed.
puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto;	then stand the woman up, gently pressing her back little by little, and then remove the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the bone structure, and return the bones with the filling.
et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor:	and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and after she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or so.
si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature;	if the fracture is to be healed, and you see, take a bladder of a goat, and tie a cane to the wound, and squeeze all the bladder back into its natural shape;
puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens:	then blow into the cane until the bladder is fully inflated inside.
la nature si revenra li brisure;	its natural shape will return to the fracture.
puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche;	And when a bone of the man or woman is broken, it should be restored as we have said for the hip bone;
et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	and these fractures should not be hidden from him who applies his study and skill, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration:	For the fracture indicates various dispositions for the right way of restoration:
enten le donques.	then understand.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge;	On a broken arrow, take a goose throat and insert it into the shaft.
puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	Then wrap it with cloth, leaving it for three days or until it heals completely.
de brisure avec plaie	from fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is important for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the bones of the leg or shoulder or similar, to be healed immediately, so that the healing which we have mentioned serves as testimony.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, but there is still a fracture from poison, if you have nothing else, then begin to restore the fracture in the same hour or on the same day, before abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the abscess increases, leave the healing until it is completely healed, as long as the abscess is calm, and do not touch it for at least a day or two, otherwise you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible through the opened heart, it is necessary that you place it gently with your hands, slightly extended.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie;	And if the extension does not appear to be even in your hands, rearrange this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width should be according to the size of the wound.
et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure;	and because it is an art to be precise, it should soak for three or four times, depending on what is required in each case of fracture.
et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	and it should be round and slightly thicker, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb in your work, and is firm in front, and thick from the middle towards the front, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent;	and it is called "palainche", so the curved bones should be placed on top of the visible joint.
et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	and twist it once, as it returns, and let them be even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, you must hold the head of the bone until the instrument has a firm grip.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir;	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, take a suitable instrument, such as a knife or scissors, in your power.
puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	then remove whoever is delayed in the bone due to stiffness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterward, knowing that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit;	if you do such that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth with astringent black wine, and wrap it carefully around it;
et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption;	and do not place any bandage or other substance on the wound that has oil, so as not to cause putrefaction and corruption.
puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure;	then administer heat as you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and clean the covering around it entirely according to the amount of the wound, and be well careful that the wound is not strained with the fracture.
et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois;	and often they have done this foolishly, and brought upon the patient either death or corruption many times.
et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	and so the tightenings should be milder and more gentle than with other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles;	And if the wound is severe or extensive, and you doubt that a bad outcome may occur, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, if it is not suitable to put pressure on it;
mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	but envelop it around, instead of pressure, with hard bandages, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound is beginning to close, then remove whatever you have placed over it, and apply healing ointment to the wound, such as a four-ingredient ointment and similar remedies.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you loosen the member twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it remains swollen and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be dislocated in such a way that the bowstring moves gently downward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it persists for a long time, and it cannot heal but keeps returning to the bowed state, knowing that there are small fragments of bone, then you must clean the wound thoroughly and remove all these misplaced fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula occurs in the place or any other form of corruption, it is necessary that you treat it according to what is said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse;	And when a bone is broken and open on the member, like the bone of the leg or the shoulder, or other similar bones of the large limbs, do not pull it, for many times death results, but let it heal until it rots.
par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues;	if, after twenty or thirty days, the wound has healed, then treat it if you can.
et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	burn injuries that come from the heat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre;	We often encounter after the healing of the break, especially when it is near a joint, and the sight of the misaligned limb is a painful thing to behold.
et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	and by chance cannot perform the natural functions of its members.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres:	Beware therefore, if it happens to us:
si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil;	if we administer astringent medicines, such as aloe, incense, myrrh, sarcocolla, sumac, and similar others, without pressing any of these things, or all together, and confide them with astringent wine, or with abundance of honey, or with ash;
et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors;	and place them on the wound in compresses, tighten them well, and do not remove them for several days;
et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee;	and then dislocate it, and begin again with another, until the nodes are healed.
ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite;	or stretch it on a well-made plank;
car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres;	because the property of the plank is such that it removes all swelling from the limbs;
et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent;	and if the node has already become hard like stone, it must be removed, cutting off the upper part and exposing the excess.
ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	You should shave it with no razor while it is infected, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after treatment.
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes:	When the fracture of the bone is healed and the limb remains weak and delicate, it occurs for many reasons:
de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit;	due to which one was tied too tightly and not tied as it should be;
ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre;	or because it had too many bindings, and cannot restore blood flow to the limb;
ou por multitude d’arosement;	or because of the abundance of inflammation;
ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre;	or due to excessive and sudden movements, not staying in place at the appropriate time;
ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	or because the patient has little blood in their body, making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui;	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat, and make the body firm, until the blood increases within them.
et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce;	and administer baths, giving joy and comfort;
puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre;	then place the poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts great nourishment, and rise it often with cold water, until the nourishment reaches the member.
et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Both members twisted after the dislocation.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil:	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the member is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural strength.
si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre;	nor believe the foolish who say one must break off the member from the very beginning, and many foolish people have done this in our land.
et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors;	and this work is blamed, and it brings great harm, and perhaps death;
toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses;	However, if inflammation and pain are severe, it is necessary to use hot water or cook gentle herbs such as fennel, roots, melilot, and similar things.
et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus;	and apply the gentle plaster, well-made as a decocion, and take the mucilaginous part of fennel, and preserve it with gelatin fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster from it.
ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	You take fat figures (or perhaps fatty substances), grind them finely with a pestle, and mix them with similar remedies that soften the hardening.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never should the dislocation be subjected to continuous and prolonged friction with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow the affected limb to move every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement;	If the stiffness is due to inflammation and hardness, similar to stone, then it must be cut open with iron, if necessary reaching up to the bone, using a delicate incision.
et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	and apply compression and study the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations result from a joint moving out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs due to no apparent reason, it is necessary to attempt to bring the limb back to its normal position immediately.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu;	For if treatment is delayed, the swelling may increase, and in some cases, it might be necessary to forcefully reset the joint back into place.
por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez:	for this reason, it is not necessary to move it as soon as it swells.
maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	often causing fatigue and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez;	nevertheless, when this happens, if it makes the patient healthier, then leave it until the abscess is completely healed.
puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	then raise the affected limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as the cure comes to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the upper limbs from the wrist to the shoulder.
des mandibules	and of the jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres:	Soon, it happens that the jaws become dislocated, and the dislocation of both occurs in two ways:
ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc;	when they are slightly out of their sockets and softens a little;
ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	or they are entirely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and draining saliva from the mouth that he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue moves with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is entirely and completely dislocated, then it is necessary that you reset it immediately, without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars;	and in such a way that the physician places his hand on the patient's head, and pulls it toward him with gentle pressure at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, so that the dislocation is from two parts.
et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal;	and the other two hands should be prepared, making them equal.
et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	and instructs the patient to soften his jaws and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And he adjusts the mirrors equally until they return to their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement;	And if they return to their place, especially when both jaws are together, then apply hot water and oil gently, until they align slightly.
ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	Do not hesitate to bring it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back equally, and the mouth of the ill person closes well without softening, place moistened cloth bands covered in a mixture of rose oil and wax on them, then gently bind them with soft strings.
