et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and make the patient sleep on their back, with their legs between two pillows, so that they do not move to the right or left, nor should they strive for more, but gently press down on the flesh until the pain is gone and the jaws are relaxed.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then massage what he wants to move lightly, and do not strain to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well closed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and do not return to their normal position, then fever and persistent aches may occur, along with abdominal pain, or vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions;	And when you see this, then know that it is destruction;
et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	and often it kills those who have it, within seven days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The fork cannot dislocate from either side in the continuity of it, and from the worst side, it is never healed properly outside, and it causes great pain.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, extends their arms;
et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra;	and then press the joint firmly into your palm, and it will return.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	then place the splint and bandage, and tighten it;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer;	and the joint which is towards the neck cannot be dislocated.
se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit;	if it does not dislocate, and if it never dislocates, then return it to its place, as we have said.
puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	then place the splint and bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	and thus, itself is brought back to the shoulder joint, when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	**Shoulder Dislocation**
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres:	Know that the shoulder is damaged in three ways:
de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz;	one is that it damages the part of the shoulder at the base;
et li seconde est a la partie dou pis;	and the second is at the part where there is most pain;
et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	and by chance, it damages the part above, and this happens seldom.
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners;	and do not dislocate it behind for the shoulder, and do not dislocate it inside for the nerves.
et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment;	and often dislocate it towards the armpit, especially those with little strength, for these leap strongly.
a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	for those with enough strength, it leaps slightly, and returns slightly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to no one that they feel a sharp pain or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of that.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains;	You should therefore test it, as long as you are certain.
et adonques encomence la cure.	and then begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And the dislocation is recognized when it moves towards the joint, and it makes a distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them a manifest diversity;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes;	and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and by pressing on the joint, the top of the shoulder feels as if it were one.
et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	and the patient cannot bring his hand back to its normal position, nor make any movement.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	and also, if it is dislocated at the top and not properly concealed, for you will feel it clearly when touching;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	and this method of dislocation is not to be used unless it is fresh, or if the patient is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu;	And the method is that the healer places his hand on top of the patient's shoulder, then places his palm beneath the joint, and pulls the joint upwards with force towards the bone.
et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz;	and the healer lifts his hand and extends it upwards, then places it beneath.
si venra hastanment.	if he comes to illness.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude;	And if it does not come as we have said, within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water.
et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	and apply gently softening and soothing treatments, such as an infusion of aloe vera, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and let it be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	then the patient should be placed on his back, and a soft cloth of equal thickness should be placed under him, neither too loose nor too tight, then place his heel on the cloth, and gently lift the head from the shoulder, and stretch the hand of the ill person.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval;	and other ministers tie the patient's head so it does not move below.
celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	the shoulder now returns, and if it is dislocated, reset it according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides;	and make sure that the person at home is stronger than the patient.
et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and be straight towards the side, and pull the patient's shoulder away from the body, lifting the shoulder up so that the patient hangs on the opposite side.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	and other assistants take hold of the patient's hand, lowering it towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, so that anything heavy causes him trouble, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere:	And it is also done in another way:
et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	and insert a long stick into the ground, making the end as sharp as a pistol, neither too thick nor too thin.
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust;	then place the patient below, but with soft cloth above, and the pain should be from the long of the leg.
puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then his hand should be extended downwards from another direction, and the joint will return to its place gently;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure:	and if it does not want to return for all the things we have said, then do this treatment:
pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	take a strip of cloth wide and long enough to cover the entire wound, and cut it in such a way that the edge can fully enter under the stitch.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide;	then lay two cloth strips over the wound to prevent further pain for the patient, and insert them under the wound of the sick person.
et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part:	and extends one arm over the leg along its length, and fastens the aid to the leg, and places the arm at the top of the hand, then puts the arm on the broad edge of a shovel, and lets the hand hang down, and leaves the body dangling from the other side:
li jointure reva ens maintenant.	the joint moves now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is dislocated in any way, it is necessary to put under the joint a thread of equal wool, then apply the plaster with a mixture of powder from the mill, with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then pull the joint back into place, and tie the bandage again on the plaster, and press the hand against the collarbone, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost;	And it is necessary that he moves little, as long as the limb is comfortable, because it will heal faster.
et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve;	and then move more after a few days or seven, and move it.
et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	and if (it) is closed and (the patient) cannot relax it, then (it) is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is firmly stuck due to moisture or any other cause, it is necessary that you apply cautery in three places, as it is described in the chapter of cautery or treatment.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis;	And if you do all this, and after seven days (the joint) becomes loose, and does not hold its place, and the patient cannot raise their arm above their head, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either compressed, stretched, or softened.
et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	and know that the joint will never return to its proper place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure;	The dislocation that is toward the worst side, and the joints, either in front or behind, are caused by a sudden movement, stretching of the hands, and (the patient) should be given another treatment.
et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and cure as long as he is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing, cracking occurs in the member, and delayed movement, if the patient uses it many times, until the cracking is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient;	Knowing that the dislocated joint is weakened at the edges and returns to its place;
et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien;	and is weakened from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not fully corrected, as we can clearly see it and feel it;
et desalue selonc chescune figure.	and is weakened according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated part with the healthy one, if you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	Because the joint is dislocated, preventing the arm from bending or touching the shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And it is necessary that you reset it so that the abscess closes and does not reappear, because if the abscess reappears, it would be difficult to reset it.
et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier;	and by chance it cannot be brought back to its original state completely, especially when it is at the rear.
si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	it is worse than other dislocations, causing greater pain, and if left untreated, it may lead to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains;	And for the restoration, when it is possible to bring it back, you extend your hand with both of yours.
et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	and the arms should be extended, and the hands turned toward the side opposite the joint, pressing and stretching it together with the palm's base, until it returns to its original position.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to its original position, and bring the base of the palm with the joint that is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer a strong extension;
et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension;	and this involves extending the arm, and the physician should hold it firm, so that it does not move during the extension.
puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	then turn the arm in each direction, after you have wrapped it with a long and wide cloth;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when you observe the joint at the hand's junction, if it is not lubricated with any oil to soften the joint, then press the swollen joint firmly, until it returns to its normal position.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in place, apply dry plaster with heat, form a strain, and stretch the arm to the collarbone of the suffering patient, and do not leave it for any days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse;	and if the joint is firmly in its place, loosen the ligament, and release it.
et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis;	and if you see that the joint is not tightly held, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave it thus for no days until it is firmly set.
puis le deslie.	then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez;	And if the patient feels pain after resetting the joint and it becomes silent, then bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is relieved.
ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	or place the greasy sheep's fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and immerse it in the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain;	and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then replace the fat and then immerse in the bath again.
et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this twice or three times, as long as it is healthy;
et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus;	and if you see, place a fine cloth dipped in warm butter over it and hold it on;
si revenra a sa disposition.	it will return to its original position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures.	The joint of the hand is misaligned, and its return to position is lighter than other joints.
Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	However, it is necessary to bring it back to its original position carefully, at the same time that it is misaligned, so that the joint does not swell or an abscess forms hot.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the re-location is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the patient's limbs, and look to ensure they are even, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu;	However, it is important that you check if it is well-positioned.
adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	then place the patient's back of his hand on a table, extending and relocating it.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on a table, and look to see where the joint appears.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If it returns now, it is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If, however, the strain of soothing treatments does not cease for abscesses, it leaves him thus without wanting to recommence.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place for any number of days, then the joint remains dislocated.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout:	and causes no harm to the patient as long as their hands are relaxed and cannot tighten anything at all:
adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere;	so you know that the nerve or artery is cut,
si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If there is no other remedy but to extract the case by delicate cautery, then it may be worth trying something else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is dislocated, if you place on it the splint that we have said, then pull and hold it for a day, then release it and leave it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well and there is no fracture, then apply hot water moistened cloth and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocation of the two joints of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	Never should the palms be massaged on either side, or the back of the hand or the belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	then they should be pressed, and the dislocation reduced with gentle movements until it returns, then support the head with both hands, and pull it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor;	and leave it for two days, then set it even with the other hand on that same day.
et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut;	and bind it with a thread, as we have said, and loosen it by day, and make it move, and replace it to the bone;
et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and do this often, while it is tight, and do the same if it becomes unwell in the palm of the hand, and proceed as you have done before, until it is healed;
et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same when it becomes unwell on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the spine
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or the collarbone is dislocated and there is no cure, the patient's condition worsens rapidly and death may ensue.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I.	And the signs are that the contractions suddenly leave without will, unable to hold it, and often a limb becomes weak, either both legs or both arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars;	And often the elderly person becomes mute from the third part onwards;
celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	The one that becomes mute at the back is called 'gibbousness'.
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance:	The treatment is that if the gibbousness has come from childhood, you must reward it.
si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	If there is no cure or recovery from it at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or impacts or similar things, they speak of old ways of treatment with great words, but it brings no real benefit at all.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the hardness that comes at the root of the hair, no one has any knowledge of it.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also those that come straight in the second side, and one cannot cure from outside unless the one that comes to the back is properly treated, as I say.
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and it is that the patient should be extended on their face in the first position evenly, and have pressure from beneath so they do not move.
puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then I insert a stick into the hollow of the earth-formed head, and another through the soft parts, and tie a strong cord around the afflicted's arms, legs, hips, and ankles.
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons;	and the two assistants know the positions of the cords, one for the head and others for the soft parts, among the two sticks;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and they should be tightly held, the sticks as we have said, and the patient places his palms on the formed spike until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three feet long, cut a slot in the wall behind it, place the patient on their side, and turn the head of the table away from the wall, then put the middle of the table over the spine.
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu;	and place the mirrors on the other side of the table's head, and press firmly until it returns to its place.
et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and if you see, do it with the turner that turns in your hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you should insert two splints into the head of the patient's ailing arm, and towards the feet, two others, with a space of about the length of a palm between each splint.
et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent;	and each splint should have an opening or a hole, through which you can insert a thread and tighten it firmly in place so that the splints do not move.
et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and between each pair of splints, there should be a connecting thread, which tightens the splints together, and this thread should be as thin as the length of a palm.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then take the ligament that is among the muscles towards the head, and the other ligament towards the feet at the other turn, and each of the assistants turns their turn to the entire ligament, and the master makes the spike even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, apply a drying plaster with plenty of heat, then the stoppers, and then the steel of a tablet three fingers long, which should hold the joint of the stiffness and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a ligament, as we have said, and use the patient's subtle relief, until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant;	and if any condition arises at the end of health, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the intent that we have said before.
et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations;	and never should one administer a plug, and never should the appearance arise in the lower spine of the back, and it is believed to be dislocation;
et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption:	and it is the bone that opens, so one must not have any presumption;
par aventure feroit venir la mort.	in case death were to come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures;	You know that the joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike other joints.
et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties:	and the hip joint is misaligned according to three parts.
dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier;	inside and outside, and front and back;
et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	and deeper inside, then less misaligned front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is such that when you join the affected leg with the healthy one, if it is longer, and opens the sick knee more than the healthy ones, and the sick cannot double their knee at the fire.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the leg that is severely inflamed with hot abscess, because the joint of the thigh comes here.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him who is about to die is that this event is contrary to what has happened before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement;	And the signs of one who has it in front, so it is that they have a well-aligned leg according to its completion;
toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	nevertheless, do not bend the knee without pain, and if one wishes to make it move, it cannot do so before, and it retains urine, and swells the leg, and as it moves, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of someone who is about to die from behind include: they cannot spread or bend their knee, and one leg is more twisted than the other, and the angle of the limb becomes soft, and the foot is in a different position compared to the hip, towards the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure;	They must reset this appearance of dislocation if it is an old dislocation that persists according to its nature, as there is no cure for it.
et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	and it is not appropriate that he should have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre;	And for the one whose dislocation is recent, and it's of the four types of dislocation—if you act quickly and reduce the joint to its proper place, both inside and aligned, and then move it to the right or left.
par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	so that if it returns, there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare a strong support, and stretch the leg strongly with both hands, or bind it to the knee joint.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe;	and other helpers extend their hand over it in such a way that they bend their fingers towards the sole of the foot, then tightly hold it with a gentle grip on the calf.
et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another holds the head with a firm grip.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they extend it upwards and downwards several times, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common to all four parts, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance.	If this is not treated, it is necessary to take care of its appearance.
Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	When dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary to have the patient lie on their healthy side, then apply a bandage at the base of the thigh, and the joint that is above the angle, then stretch the bandage towards the angle and towards the strength.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment:	then apply pressure with other assistants on the patient's arms, embrace the large joint of the injured thigh, and extend it to a wider opening.
si revenra a son leu maintenant;	if it returns to its place now;
et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner we have said, then you should bind both feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature on both heels and both knees, and let the affected leg be extended two fingers more than the others.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc;	then it should be hung from the top of a post, and two long arms should be above the ground.
puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then instruct the healer to embrace the top of the thigh, and have other assistants with the patient, who also embrace the thigh, for the joint now moves gently.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is in the exterior, if the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of kyphosis, then tighten the ligaments on the affected leg properly, and also on the opposite side.
puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then place two pins, one at the top and another at the bottom, then insert a pin between the thighs of the patient in the shape.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	and he should surround it with moist flags, so that he does not harm the patient, and then extend each limb towards him, and with your eyes make the dislocation equal in his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it does not return, put it on a table and press it as we have said in the previous section, and lay the patient on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit;	And when the dislocation is present, it is necessary to extend the diseased leg forcibly, as I have said;
et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	and place the mirror to his pain of being on the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and stretch it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches;	And if the dislocation is external, it is not necessary to stretch the patient downwards, nor raise him up from the ground, but rather he should be kept in a position as if his hip was dislocated downward, just as we have said gently on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and place it on his face, with the ligament extended as we have said before, and he must press down on the joint on the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz;	and will be at the point when the patient extends his legs, and they will be even.
adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	then fasten the thighs, and apply the plaster, and wrap a bandage tightly so that the hip does not move.
et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus;	and rest for three or four days, then untie it, and apply the plaster again.
et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors;	and if you see them grow even, stretch them as they were before, and leave it for three days.
puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then release it, and make it go smoothly, as long as the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From the dislocation of the knee.
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The patient is dislocated in three ways:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	that is to say, internally and externally, and behind.
et ne desalue point devant.	and do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are such that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if they cannot straighten it at the knee, know that they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all is such that you make the patient sit straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place them face down on your lap, and place their foot on top of yours.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	then take their knee in your palms, and draw it between your fingers, then bend both sides of the knee forming an 'L'.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	and other assistants stretch his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he has safely freed his leg slightly.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	and apply a poultice, and make the leg move at the knee, and hold it together strongly for three or four days, then loosen it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and the patient should not move about until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, apply firm extension as we have said in the treatment of the neck, as long as it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	On the dislocation of the heel.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heel is neither completely dislocated nor fully healed, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the sign is that the ankle is swollen, and it feels tense in the area where it is dislocated.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	We reset it if it is light, and one must gently extend their hands when they are slightly stunned.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, one must then ensure the patient lies straight and holds the limb firmly above the ankle with a helper.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then take the foot in your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then stretch it upwards, and gently bend the foot upwards.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	and do this twice as we have said, both bending and stretching the foot.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that's good.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	If it does not return, the work must be recommenced, for it will;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in that way, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and insert a stick firmly into the earth between their legs, binding the blankets around them to prevent injury to the patient.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	then attend to the patient's leg, and have other assistants stretch the foot or hold it in place, securing it to the collar of the bed.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	then extend each limb equally, and let them move repeatedly between the legs of the patient to hold the patient still when they are stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	then place the mirrors equally on the dislocated joint in both hands, and another helper holds the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return to its place firmly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it stops bleeding, apply a poultice and compress above, and strain the limb, fasten the foot to the leg, and secure the stirrups behind the ankle, ensuring the bindings are not too tight.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	then let it be for two or three days, and gently move it if it is tight.
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	then on the third or fourth day, gently release it, and make the patient walk for three days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	and if it goes beyond this limit, it is not fortunate that it does not dislocate further.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it is necessary to soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, while it remains healthy.
des dois	Of the two (parts/sides).
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two (parts/sides) are disaligned, if they need to be properly aligned without strain, it is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is in any other part of the foot or leg, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back or on a table straight, and place your foot on what opens these joints, then press with your foot firmly until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	and when it is even, and it opens nothing, he places the sole of the foot on a table with two joints, then strains it firmly, and leaves it for three days, then loosens it.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and makes it rest, as long as it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	from wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, often the patient dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not presumptuous in treatment, since you are ignorant of the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not patient and merciful and slow, do not be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and at the beginning of things, apply hot poultices to the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you have no hope for recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and if you see hope, then immediately reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess does not form again;
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	and when the limb is in place, apply hot poultices to the abscess and treat the wound as necessary with dried herbs;
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	and if there is a dislocation with broken bones and small fragments, then as we have said in simple diseases;
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	and keep yourself from entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, for it is your movement according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your arms and body.
